Resolution of the Fuzhou Military-Civilian Conflict Case 60

Huian Again Incites Great Change Due to Levying Tobacco Tax

Fuzhou Correspondence: Although the military-civilian conflict in Fuqing County was stopped by Liu Jun, the regimental commander of the Second Regiment of the Second Mixed Brigade of the Provincial Defense Forces, who led the You Baoying and Li Yunrong rain battalions, Lin Jing, the captain of the Second Independent Detachment of the Provincial Defense Forces, demanded compensation of 250,000 yuan because his troops lost two battalion's worth of military equipment and more than thirty battalion, company, and platoon leaders were killed in action during the incident. The Rescue Township Corps of Gaoshan and Longtian towns, however, argued that the villages had been repeatedly looted by Lin's troops and were unbearably trampled on. Unless they were transferred, the local area would never have peace. Both sides went to extremes and could not be resolved. Various groups in Fuqing County then sent Chen Ruyi and others to the province to petition the Security Office of the Provincial Government, requesting a swift resolution to avoid another war and further devastation of the local area. The Provincial Government then put forward a discussion at the committee meeting on the 19th, believing that Lin Jing had repeatedly harassed the local area and repeatedly ignored warnings, which was a violation of military discipline. It was decided to dismiss him from his post for investigation, and the troops under his command were to be separately reorganized by the Second Mixed Brigade of the Provincial Defense Forces. If there were any who fled to various places, the local garrison and militia were allowed to intercept and disarm them at any time. As for the post-disaster matters in Fuqing, Lin Zhiyuan, a member of the Provincial Committee, and Zhou Xiaopei, the brigade commander of the Second Mixed Brigade of the Provincial Defense Forces, were recommended to handle the matter properly. As soon as Lin Jing heard the news, he led his troops out of the county seat at 12:00 that evening, taking the road to Dongzhang Town and intending to go to Yongtai. Upon receiving the report, Liu Jun immediately led the You and Li battalions to pursue and attack, killing more than fifty people, capturing more than sixty people, and seizing more than a hundred guns. Lin Jing led the remnants to escape to Yongtai. On the 20th, the Provincial Government had telegraphed the Yongtai garrison Huang Bingwu's troops to intercept them. The Fuqing incident was finally resolved. However, the troops of Chen Guohui of the Second Mixed Brigade of the Provincial Defense Forces stationed in Huian County shot and killed eight farmers and seriously injured more than ten farmers in Batou Township in the northern district of the county on the 15th of this month due to the forced imposition of a tobacco seedling tax, which aroused public outrage. More than ten thousand people immediately gathered to surround and disarm Chen's troops and destroy the Measurement Bureau (the agency in charge of the tobacco seedling tax). Upon receiving the news, Chen Guohui immediately transferred a large team from Quanzhou to suppress them. The two sides are currently engaged in fierce fighting. Upon receiving the report, the Provincial Government telegraphed yesterday to stop it. (January 21)

Wuhan Disaster Victims Given Deadline to Move Out of the Urban Area 61

Hankou Correspondence: According to recent investigations, there are indeed more than 300,000 disaster victims in Wuhan, most of whom are elderly, weak, women, and children, and their suffering is even greater. This is because the young and strong have gradually moved elsewhere to make a living on their own. The elderly, weak, women, and children have no work to do, so they have nowhere to return. Their living difficulties are especially pitiful. They eat chaff and wear rags. They live in streets and alleys. Under the wind and snow, hundreds and thousands of people sell their wives and children, which is common everywhere. The hell on earth is probably not enough to describe their suffering. Recently, the Post-Disaster Relief Committee, in view of the large number of disaster victims, decided that not only are the relief funds too small to be sustainable, but also fears that bandits will mix in and affect public security. It was decided to issue relief once and no longer issue it in the future, and a new relief area was designated, requiring all disaster victims to move there, otherwise the military and police agencies would enforce it. The Pacification Office, the Wuhan Garrison Headquarters, the Hubei Flood Relief Committee, and the Hubei Provincial Government jointly issued a notice limiting the time from the 23rd to the end of the month, to completely move out of the urban area within a week. The notice is as follows: "The principle of investigating and handling relief is that it is better to disperse than to gather. Moreover, during the winter defense period, with hundreds of thousands of disaster victims gathered in Wuhan, it is difficult to guarantee that bandits will not mix in and attempt to do wrong. However, the situation of the genuine disaster victims is extremely pitiful. Therefore, in the absence of a way to handle it, we have devised a two-pronged approach. It has been decided to move the existing disaster victims in the three towns of Wuchang, Hanyang, and Xia to a place farther away from the city. On the one hand, the place is remote to avoid mixing, and on the other hand, the situation is scattered to avoid crowding. Seven articles have been discussed and decided, listed below. This is to ensure the thorough relief purpose and the safety and order of the local area, and we will do what we say. Disaster victims must comply with it without violation. 1) The originally announced relief of 20 catties of wheat per disaster victim will now be issued half by the committee within a week, and the remaining 10 catties will be issued at the newly designated location. 2) No relief will be given in Wuhan in the future. 3) The winter relief of this committee will be suspended. 4) A new relief location has been designated, but no shelter will be built. Those who have already lived in the shelters of this committee can freely dismantle and move them, but they must not dismantle them arbitrarily, causing disputes. 5) The new relief location, such as those originally in the Hushan area of Hanyang, will be designated as the area between Caidian and Xinglongji under the jurisdiction of the county. Those in Hankou will be designated as the area between Hengdian and Qijiawan under the jurisdiction of Huangpi. Those in Hongshan, Meijiashan, Luojiashan, Changchun Guan, and various places in the provincial capital will be designated as the area near Jinkou under the jurisdiction of Wuchang. Although the relocation will not be out of the above areas, the disaster victims can choose an area closer to their original place of origin to move into, so that it will be easier to return to their hometowns in the future. 6) The newly built places will be requested by the committee to the Pacification Office to dispatch troops to be stationed there permanently for protection. 7) From the date of the notice, the victims will be limited to seven days to move to the new relief location. Those who refuse to move will be forcibly enforced by the military and police. (January 21)

The Calamity of War and Banditry in Huangpi 62

Hankou Correspondence: Huangpi was previously attacked by rampant bandits, and the county seat was in imminent danger. After the suppression by various armies, the banditry gradually subsided. However, before they could catch their breath, Li Mingzhong's troops suddenly changed, and the inside and outside of the city suffered considerable losses. Even now, order has not been restored. At the same time, the bandit forces have returned after their departure. If there is an opportunity, the future disaster is still unknown. Therefore, the course of the mutiny and the current situation of the Red bandits are recorded as follows, according to what I have heard. First, the Red bandits attacked the city and were defeated, and fled back to

Huang'an. The troops that came to suppress them were mostly temporarily conscripted, each with its own defense area. After the bandits left, they returned to their defense areas. Huangpi County was still guarded by Li Mingzhong's troops of the 30th Division. The brigades of Li's division have always been uncoordinated, and Li has not been to the army for a long time. Wang Zhenhuai, Chief of Staff of the Governor's Office, acted on his behalf. Recently, the local clans changed the brigade commander of a certain brigade, and the rift became more apparent. The disaster occurred on the 17th. In the beginning of the incident, a small part of Li's Special Service Brigade opened the east gate of the county seat and fled towards Macheng. At dawn on the 18th, the 88th and 89th Brigades rushed to Huangpi from Huang'an and completely disarmed the troops of the Special Service Brigade that had not yet left the city. In the afternoon of the same day, soldiers inside and outside the city clashed, and at the same time, more than a hundred stores were looted. After Wang Zhenhuai and others tried their best to suppress them, they gradually subsided. However, until the 20th, the city gates had not been opened, and the stores had not resumed business. A certain councilor sent by the Pacification Office and Liu Weiyuan, the newly appointed magistrate of Huangpi, had both arrived at the county seat and had been meeting with Chief of Staff Wang of the Governor's Office and local gentry and businessmen for days to discuss post-disaster matters. Local order will be restored within days. As for Li Mingzhong, who was recuperating in Wuhan, he refused to see guests from the time the incident occurred. The next day, he took a boat to Shanghai for recuperation. The position of Commander of the 30th Division was taken over by Peng Zhenshan, sent by the Pacification Office, and the position of Deputy Commander was held concurrently by Wang Cibai, commander of the 22nd Route Special Service Brigade. The Governor's Office was still acting on behalf of Wang Zhenhuai. At the time of the mutiny, the bandits who had fled back to Huang'an thought there was an opportunity and made a comeback, causing Changxuanling, Baishuigang, Chenjiawan, Liujiaqiao, Wangjiahe, Hengshan, Luohan Temple, and Xilijiaji to become bandit areas again. According to people from Huangpi, the Red bandits conscripted young farmers into the Red Guards wherever they went, and conscripted old and weak women and children into the basket teams. The Red Guards were the vanguard, and the formal Red Army was the cover. Therefore, when the army suppressed the bandits, most of those who died were genuine farmers, and the Red Army suffered less losses. At the moment, the main force of the bandits is in Wanshan Temple and Changlinggang in the northeast, and the pseudo-Soviet government is set up in Hekou, at the junction of Beixiangwei and Huang'an and Luoshan in Henan. With Changlinggang, Baliawan, Pujiazhai, and Caijiawan as corners, the situation is extremely consolidated. If the bandit lair is not quickly destroyed, it is feared that it will eventually become a problem on the border between Hubei, Henan, and Anhui. (January 21)

Abrupt Decrease in the Number of Emigrants from Chao and Shan 63

Last year saw a reduction of more than half compared to the year before.

Shantou correspondence: The population of Chaozhou and Meizhou is prolific, and approximately 150,000 to 160,000 people migrate to the Nanyang Islands each year. Since 1928, Nanyang has been affected by the global economic downturn, leading to sluggish sales of local products, a daily increase in unemployed workers, soaring exchange rates, and tepid commerce in various ports. On August 1, 1930, the British colonial government of Singapore issued an order prohibiting the entry of Chinese laborers. Initially, it permitted the entry of 2,321 individuals per month, limited to the four ports of Xiamen, Hong Kong, Haikou, and Shantou. On October 1, 1931, the quota for Chinese entry was further reduced to 1,160. Shantou received only 400 passenger tickets per month among the four ports. Due to the restricted number of passenger tickets, various shipping companies diverted their ships to other ports. It is reported that starting on the first of this month, Singapore will continue to issue the seventh restriction order on the entry of Chinese laborers. This is the biggest blow suffered by our country's immigrants to Nanyang and a great misfortune for those from Chaozhou and Meizhou seeking a livelihood.

Secondly, the Dutch East Indies has increased the entry tax for Chinese, curbing the entry of Chinese laborers. Ten years ago, Chinese going to Batavia and the Java Islands initially paid a landing tax of 25 guilders per person. This was later increased to 50 guilders, then to 100 guilders in 1929, and further increased to 150 guilders starting on April 1, 1931. Moreover, it must be carried with the individual and paid upon landing, otherwise landing is not permitted. Even after paying the tax, a stamp of guarantee from local businesses is still required for the individual to freely engage in employment and seek a livelihood. Since the promulgation of this rule, those from Chaozhou and Meizhou seeking a livelihood in the Dutch territories are almost in dire straits.

Thirdly, there is the new immigration regulation issued by the Siamese government on August 1, 1930. Starting in November, all Chinese entering the country must pay a tax of 80 baht per person. Those who have not obtained a local exit passport or proven their nationality will not be allowed to enter. Furthermore, an annual head tax of 10 baht must be paid. After the implementation of this rule, the burden on the hundreds of thousands of overseas Chinese in Siam has become heavier, and it has become more difficult to make a living.

Fourthly, Annam (Vietnam), Saigon, also promulgated new regulations last year. All new arrivals must pay a landing license fee of 15 yuan at the New Immigrant Office. However, this license is not valid in areas such as Hanoi. Restrictions on the movement of overseas Chinese are very strict. In addition to paying the head tax each year, Chinese must also pay a remittance tax, making it almost impossible for them to sustain themselves.

In summary, the Chinese government is indifferent to these various situations. Without effective relief, overseas Chinese are unable to unite and improve their environment. Last year, Shantou frequently received unemployed Chinese laborers deported from various parts of Nanyang. Their gaunt and discolored appearance was extremely miserable. These returning overseas Chinese were mostly sent back to their hometowns with half-fare tickets for boats and trains, obtained from the municipal government through the Overseas Chinese Mutual Aid Society. It is reported that last year, due to soaring exchange rates, overseas Chinese remittances back to Shantou were approximately 40 million yuan, compared to over 50 million yuan in the previous year. Based on the amount of exchange rates, the foreign capital flowing into the interior decreased by more than half last year (the value of one Singapore dollar was 1.4 yuan in national currency the previous year, while it was 2.2 to 2.6 yuan last year). This issue is of great importance to the livelihood of the people of Chaozhou and Meizhou. This is because many of those who remitted money back to Shantou last year were small-scale overseas Chinese capitalists who, unable to operate in Nanyang, sold off their existing

productive enterprises and returned with the funds, which is not comparable to the previous year when most remittances were from workers supporting their families. It is reported that in 1930, the number of people leaving Shantou for Nanyang was 115,791, and the number returning to the country was 93,767. After various places restricted the entry of Chinese laborers in 1931, the number of overseas Chinese departing from Shantou was

58,238, and the number returning to the country was 65,866, which is the opposite. There is an unprecedented situation where the number of entries exceeds the number of exits. This is a serious problem today. (17th day)

Financial Urgency in Zhenjiang 64

Zhenjiang is located at the intersection of north and south of the Yangtze River, and its commerce has always been prosperous. Since the opening of the Tianjin-Pukou Railway caused changes in the terrain, it has gradually declined. In the last ten years, the situation has become even more desolate due to the siltation of the riverbanks and the failure of wheeled vehicles to connect. Passengers and goods are transferred through Huojiaqiao, and merchants and travelers move with the passengers and goods, resulting in an even more depressed situation for various industries. Last year's flood in Jiangbei caused the only remaining wholesale trade in Jiangbei to be interrupted. Although efforts have been made to recover outstanding debts, it is difficult to collect them in full. Although there are no precise statistics on the direct and indirect losses suffered by the business community due to the flood, it is estimated to be over one million, which has caused a financial panic in the city. Foreign silver has risen to 69 fen, and standard silver has risen to over 960 taels. The silver exchange rate has risen to 60 fen, which is a rare phenomenon. In the past week, although the prices of foreign silver and standard silver have not reached new highs, no one is willing to sell spot silver or standard silver at the market price. The daily quotations of the Money Trade Association are merely for show, and there is actually no transaction. The deposits and debts of money shops have always been based on the Erqi Bao banknotes. The Erqi Bao banknotes can only be used for book entries in the city. If it is necessary to repay debts to other places, it is necessary to exchange them for spot silver or purchase Shenyuan banknotes. It is necessary to negotiate with the corresponding money shops and add a certain amount to the market price. Only small amounts can be handled, but large amounts are difficult to fulfill. In view of this situation, various shops do not dare to deposit money in money shops after receiving payments or selling goods. They prepare to remit accounts to other places through banks, so the financial situation is even more stagnant. The relief measures previously agreed upon by the government and business, such as a bank loan of 500,000 yuan that can be cashed immediately, the Money Trade Association drawing out 1 million yuan in discounted bills, of which half has already been drawn, and the provincial government borrowing and allocating 1 million yuan in construction public bonds that are still pending mortgage of cash, and how to coordinate them, are also pending research and handling. However, there are not many days left until the end of the year, and the financial situation is still as stagnant as before. If relief is delayed further, the market situation will be difficult to be optimistic about in the future.

Local Correspondence

Fengxian 65

A Tragic Eyegouging Incident Occurs in Nantai Riqiao: In the north of Nantai Riqiao, which is part of our county, there is a farmer named Shen Jiasheng, who has always been brutal and extremely domineering, and therefore

has accumulated deep grievances from the outside world. Last night, he returned from town, and before he had even sat down, many people came to his house to inquire. Shen's wife opened the door to receive them, and those people went straight into the inner room and took out sharp knives to completely gouge out both of his eyes. His wife rushed to save him, but they had already escaped. The next morning, she reported the incident to the local public security substation. Inspector Shen went to examine the scene and found that Jiasheng's left eyeball was protruding from its socket, and the other eyeball had been completely gouged out. There was blood everywhere, and the scene was extremely tragic. The inspector has now submitted a report on the incident to the county government, requesting the arrest of the perpetrators and their punishment.

Songjiang 66

A Case of Alimony Leading to Serious Injury and Litigation: Fei Shiqing, who moved to Songjiang from the 14th District, had an affair with a certain widow in the past and lived together for a time. They had a daughter, but their feelings gradually faded due to other reasons, and they eventually separated. The woman filed a lawsuit in court, and the court ruled that Fei Shiqing should pay the woman a certain amount of alimony each year for a period of 25 years. Recently, Fei suddenly stopped making payments. The woman went to Fei's residence on the 23rd evening to demand the fulfillment of the judgment, which led to an argument. The woman wanted to move her own furniture, but Fei refused to allow it and pushed the woman out of the door. The woman fell heavily and her occipital bone struck the threshold, causing her skin to break and bleed. She called the police and was sent to the bureau. Because the woman's injuries were not minor, she was first sent to St. Joseph's Hospital for treatment. The doctor said that she had a concussion and there was a risk of danger. After bandaging her wound, she was sent back to the Public Security Bureau. This morning, she was sent to the court's procuratorate for interrogation. The official ordered the defendant, Fei Shiqing, to be detained for investigation. The injured person was sent to Songjiang County Hospital for treatment.

Kunshan 67

Lujiaqiao Town Robbed by Bandits: Lujiaqiao Town, located ten miles from the city, was suddenly attacked by four bandit boats at around 9:00 PM on the 22nd. The bandits, numbering more than 30, spoke with an Anhui accent and were armed with guns. After landing, six bandits fired shots into the air to demonstrate their power, stormed into the defense enclosure, and stole all the firearms of the regiment. They then cut the telephone lines and joined the other bandits to rob the entire town for two hours. Not satisfied with their plunder, they also kidnapped three children of Chen Jingren, the owner of the Chen Dachang Provisions Store, as well as Chen Mengxian, a worker at the rice mill, and Zhu Xiangqi, a pharmacist, and took them to the boats, roaring towards Zhou Shu. After the Public Security Bureau learned of the incident, they sent police officers, along with provincial water police, county police, and business groups, to suppress the bandits, but they had already gone far away. They are now searching for them separately, but it is unknown whether they will be captured.

Five-Day Extension for the Business Community's Year-End Settlement Period: The various industry associations in Kunshan, in view of the approaching deadline for the year-end settlement at the end of January, and the fact that accounts in the city and countryside were affected by the great flood last year, making it difficult to close accounts on time, felt it was necessary to grant an extension. They jointly submitted a request to the County Chamber of Commerce for relief. After the Executive Committee of the Chamber discussed the matter, they granted an extension of five days due to special circumstances and submitted a report to the county government for record.

Wuxi 68

County Orders Urgent Filing for Business Tax: The Jiangsu Provincial Department of Finance issued a special order to the business tax bureaus of various counties yesterday, stating that business tax should be effectively rectified starting from January of the 21st year in order to increase tax revenue. It has been resolved by the provincial government to formulate rectification measures and issue them to the county bureaus for compliance. Regarding the investigation of the business volume and capital of various merchants, the declaration forms that need to be filled out must have a fixed format in order to unify them. In addition to being distributed, the format of the forms is hereby sent. The county bureau director should comply, quickly prepare them from the bureau, distribute them to various merchants for filling out according to the format, and send staff to re-examine them to ensure accuracy. Business investigation certificates should be issued to each household and hung on the storefront for inspection. A report should be made according to the deadline without delay, or else there will be severe punishment. The Business Tax Collection Bureau of our county has already complied and handled the matter after receiving the order.

Bandits Open Fire and Wound Police Officer: Liu Shide, the director of the 8th Sub-bureau of the Zhouxinzhen Public Security Bureau, in view of the fact that during the winter defense period, it is inevitable that bandits will be hiding in the countryside, especially organized a winter defense patrol team that departs every night to conduct patrols. At around 10:00 PM on the afternoon before yesterday, Inspector Wu Huang of the bureau led six police officers on patrol in the jurisdiction. When they arrived at the entrance of Qianjia Lane, they suddenly saw two people wearing short clothes inside the lane, talking in whispers, which was very suspicious. As they were about to interrogate them, the two bandits pulled out pistols and shot at the police officers, causing Police Officer Chen Yan to be shot in the left arm, falling to the ground in extreme pain. Seeing that they had caused trouble, the bandits fled. Inspector Wu immediately gave chase but was unable to catch them. The injured police officer was taken back to the bureau and sent to the city yesterday to the Pure Benevolence Hospital for treatment. Fortunately, the injury was still minor and there was no danger to his life. Liu, the director of the sub-bureau, has reported the matter to the general bureau for investigation.

Changzhou 69

Bandits Rob in a Bustling Market: The Chen Hengyi Jewelry Store on Nanda Street in the city of Wuyi was visited by a customer wearing short clothes at around 11:00 AM on the 23rd, claiming to want to buy a gold ring. The shop assistant took out five rings for him to choose from. Unexpectedly, he seized the opportunity to grab three rings and flee south. The shop assistants and others followed him and chased him outside, and nearby police officers also joined in the pursuit. When they reached the Shijia Lane, the bandit knew that there were troops stationed ahead, so he threw the gold ring to the ground and fled. However, he was still caught. Because the shop assistants and others did not want to pursue the matter further, the bandit seized the opportunity to escape again.

Ransom Kidnappers Executed by Firing Squad: Jin Yuli, the head of Jinjia Village in Tanshuxiang, the 5th District of Wuyi County, and his son Baisheng were kidnapped by bandits on the night of October 31st of last year. Baisheng was later released, but Jin Yuli was not released after repeated negotiations for a ransom, and was eventually killed by the bandits. His body was divided into six pieces. After an investigation by the villagers, it was discovered that he had been killed by the kidnappers. Police detectives searched everywhere and eventually arrested a suspect named Qian Shunquan in Wuxi. He confessed to the crime. County Magistrate Zhang intended to sentence him to death and submitted a request to the provincial government, which was approved on the 21st. The criminal was immediately taken, his identity was verified, and he was taken to the Fengweidun execution ground to be executed by firing squad.

Jiangyin 70

The Provisional Court Interrogates Zhao Desheng: Zhao Desheng (nicknamed "Thief Desheng"), who lives in the Liujiaqiao area of Huazhu Township, has committed serious crimes repeatedly. He was arrested the year before and interrogated repeatedly. He was sentenced to seven years of imprisonment by the High Court for counter-revolutionary activities. Zhao refused to accept the sentence and appealed to the Supreme Court, which sent the case back to the High Court for retrial. Because this case must be handled in accordance with the Emergency Punishment Law for Undermining the Republic of China, the High Court sent it back to the original county to organize a provisional court for trial. On the 22nd, County Magistrate Ma submitted a request to the High Court for approval and commissioned Bao Lunfang, an assessor from Jingjiang, as the judge, who, together with County Magistrate Ma and Assessor Wu, convened a hearing. He also ordered the police to summon more than 20 victims, including Chen Xiangan, to court to testify. Only Jin Pu was present, proving that Zhao was a long-time bandit who participated in the Hou Shengyangkou riot seventeen years ago and was in league with the bandit leader Mao Xueqin, who had already been executed. Zhao Desbao, Zhao's uncle, Zhao Sunshi, Zhao's aunt, and Ziwen, a neighbor, all provided written evidence of Zhao's banditry, but Zhao firmly denied it, only admitting to being a thief. The interrogation was concluded, and he was taken into custody to await the recording of his confession and the review of the files before a judgment is prepared and submitted to the High Court.

The Security Corps Arrests Gamblers and Injures People in Huangtang: The Huangtang Security Corps went to Gao'an Wang Village on the evening of the 21st to suppress gambling but was unsuccessful. Team leader Xu Zongcheng led the team back and passed through Gao'an Town. They arrested three gamblers at Zhang Yuqing's teahouse. On the way back, Zhang rang a gong, alarming the villagers, who mistakenly thought they were kidnapping bandits and snatched the three gamblers, injuring three members of the Security Corps. Squad leader Gao Jinkang's pistol was snatched. Zhao Shiming, the district security chief, reported the matter to the county government on the 23rd for handling.

The Water Police Detectives Seize a Large Amount of Opium: Wang Yougui and Lu Zhi, detectives from the 5th District of the Jiangsu Provincial Water Police, recently seized two opium traffickers while going down to the water of the Jianghua steamboat of the China Merchants Bureau. Jiaxing 73

Fuxing Rice Store on Dongda Street Robbed: The Fuxing Rice Store on Dongda Street in Jiaxing was visited by three people wearing gray uniforms at 6:00 PM on the afternoon before yesterday, claiming to buy rice. The owner was unsuspecting and called the sleeping apprentice, Wang Jusheng (15 years old), to open the door and let the three people in. He then went downstairs to measure the rice. are investigating the case and conducting a thorough investigation.

Cao Wu Villagers Engage in Armed Clashes Due to Petty Disputes: The customs of the people in Wuli, a southern township in Suishan, have always been known for their strength. Some said he was a worker of the Yu family in Caowu and was suspected of being beaten to death by the Qian family. It is heard that they are preparing to engage in armed clashes again.

Taizhou 75

A Robbery Occurs in Badie: The home of Fang Laoliu, a farmer in Badie, West Township of Linhai, was broken into by more than a dozen thieves at around 12:00 PM last night. They threatened him with guns and robbed him of clothing, silver dollars, etc., for a total of 200 yuan.

Letter Received

Letter from Wang Zilan and Others from Fengxian 76

Recently, domestic newspapers have been reporting on the mutiny of the 3rd Cavalry Division stationed in Fengxian and the robbery of various agencies and the Agricultural and Industrial Bank. We are surprised to hear this. The 3rd Cavalry Division has been stationed in Fengxian for several months now. Their discipline is strict, and the relationship between the military and the people is harmonious. The cause of this incident was purely a temporary problem with the local handling of the division's supplies. A few troublemakers took the opportunity to disrupt and incite the villagers, and after a long time, misunderstandings arose. The losses of various agencies and the Agricultural and Industrial Bank reported by the outside world are not true. However, the guns, ammunition, and horses of the police team of the County Public Security Bureau are still temporarily stored in the division's armory for safety reasons. Both sides have now reached a mutual understanding, the previous grudges have been removed, and all those detained have been released one after another. The guns, ammunition, and horses will be returned immediately. They shook hands and reconciled as before. After this incident, senior officials from various party and government agencies have conducted thorough investigations, and the truth has become clear. All rumors have been dispelled. Various agencies are still operating as usual, and the military and the people are living in peace. In addition to reporting this situation to the central government, the provincial government, and the Jiangsu Pacification Commissioner's Office, we are specifically telegraphing to correct the record. Wang Zilan of the Fengxian Education Bureau, Feng Shouxin of the Construction Bureau, Dong Yushu of the Public Security Bureau, Peng Shiheng, the Secretary-General of the Farmers' Association, and Hu Xiaomin, the Chairman of the Chamber of Commerce, respectfully.

Local News

Explosion of a Small Launch Transporting Explosives at the Arsenal 77

Aged Explosives Suspected of Being Ignited by a Spark

The Da Zhong Launch and Tugboat Were Blown to Dust

Only Kuai Xianfa Survived Out of More Than Thirty People

Fishing Boats and Nearby Houses Were Also Affected

Yesterday afternoon at 3:30 PM, a violent explosion suddenly occurred on the Jiang surface west of Rihui Port outside the South City, and outside the Beipiao Wharf. The loud noise, black smoke billowed into the sky. Windows and houses dozens of miles away were shaken. The whole city was in a state of panic for a time, and rumors abounded. After investigation, it was learned that an arsenal barge transporting explosives had exploded carelessly in the Huangpu River. More than thirty people died, and only one person was rescued, who was also seriously injured. The small launch transporting explosives and two barges were all sunk. The total loss is immeasurable. The details are recorded separately as follows:

Transporting Explosives The Shanghai Arsenal needs explosive materials. The arsenal launches "Da Zhong" and "Song Yun" are used to transport them to the gunpowder depot in Laoshu Sha, Pudong. As a rule, they are loaded once a week and dispatched by arsenal launches. Yesterday was the same. The General Affairs Section of the Arsenal ordered the small Da Zhong launch to hire four civilian barges the night before, load more than one hundred boxes of shells and gunpowder (which the arsenal workers habitually call "black powder"), and transport them from Pudong to Shanghai for use in two batches.

Explosion in the Huangpu River Yesterday afternoon, the small Da Zhong launch towed barges to Pudong to load the black explosives. First, two barges loaded 55 boxes of explosives, which were towed by the small Da Zhong launch to the West Battery Wharf and unloaded at around 1:00 PM. The unloading was completed at around 2:00 PM, and the launch returned to the Pudong Wharf at 3:00 PM. At this time, the remaining two barges had loaded 45 boxes of explosives, and the launch towed them out again at 3:20 PM. At 3:30 PM, when it arrived at the Jiang surface outside the Beipiao Wharf in Rihui Port, there was a sudden explosion, and thick smoke billowed into the sky. The ammunition on the tugboat was completely destroyed by the explosion, and the two barges were blown to pieces. The Da Zhong launch also sank instantly. However, according to the message from the Garrison Headquarters, the department's investigation report stated that the small Da Zhong launch towed two barges, carrying a total of more than one hundred boxes of explosives, and so on.

Navy Rescue After the launch was bombed, the Navy Guard Battalion Water Patrol Team had not yet learned the truth, so it suspected that an accident had occurred. It immediately dispatched Wanhe, Jiangkang, and Ansan small launches, led by Deputy Team Leader Wang, along with more than a dozen guards, to the scene. The time was 3:35 PM. However, at that time, the Da Zhong launch and the two barges it was towing had been completely destroyed by the explosion. All the personnel on the Da Zhong launch and barges had been tragically killed. The Water Patrol Team only rescued Kuai Xianfa, the second mate of Da Zhong, from the Huangpu River. At around 5:00 PM, the Wanhe launch also recovered a corpse, which was Wang Zhuangda, the stoker of Da Zhong. Last night, the dead were placed at the Navy Wharf, and the arsenal notified their families. Meanwhile, the Wanhe launch was still salvaging.

Cause of the Accident According to the research of the arsenal staff who witnessed this bizarre incident, yesterday's wind was a northwest wind, and it was quite strong. When the Da Zhong launch was towing into the Huangpu River, the smoke from the launch's chimney was blown towards the barges behind due to the wind. The smoke contained sparks. These explosives had been stored for too long and were prone to explosion. Coupled with the warm weather in recent days, various unfortunate reasons combined, the explosives exploded. According to the Datong News Agency, the reason for the explosion of the shells and gunpowder in the boat this time, according to the most reliable observation, was that the "black powder" was stored during the Qing Xuantong period. It had been a long time, and its properties were very dry. At that time, the medicine boxes were not very carefully made, and they were only made of local wood. The wood was dry and shrunk, resulting in box seams. Although the arsenal used paper to paste the box seams, it was not satisfactory. After being loaded into the barges, the cables were attached to the back of the Da Zhong launch and towed. The Da Zhong launch was small, causing smoke and fire to emerge from the chimney and drift into the seams of the medicine boxes, resulting in a sudden outbreak that could not be contained.

Accident to Fishing Boats When the explosives exploded, the sound was like a giant cannon, and black smoke filled the sky. The river water in Huangpu was boiling. Two nearby fishing boats were thrown more than ten feet high due to the force of the explosion. They immediately capsized, and the men, women, old and young in the boats were buried in the Huangpu River. There was also a sailboat that was ignited by sparks from the explosives and immediately burned. Fortunately, it was rescued immediately, only destroying a sail. The stern of the Da Zhong launch was bombarded violently, and its iron anchor flew up several feet, hitting the glass windows on the third floor of the Yitaixing Coal Yard inside the Beipiao Wharf, causing great damage. Fortunately, no one was injured.

Walls Damaged and Windows Broken During the explosion, the sound was heard for dozens of miles. Residents in the South City and the French Concession felt a very strong earthquake. Many houses near Gaochang Temple collapsed. A section of the wall of Nanyang Middle School on Longhua Road collapsed. At that time, the students did not know the truth and returned home. The glass windows of shops in the Nanshi area, such as the Fuan Company in Xiaodongmen, were shattered.

Number of Casualties Due to the short time yesterday, there are no accurate statistics on the number of casualties. According to the arsenal, the number of victims is at least about 30. The small Da Zhong launch had a total of seven employees: Captain Qian Runjin, Chief Mate Gu Yuesheng, Second Mate Kuai Xianfa, Sailor Yuan Yicai, Wei Asi, Wang Zhuangda, and Wang Jinkun. Yuan Yicai was on sick leave and was not killed. Only Kuai Xianfa was rescued. None of the ten or so boatmen on the other two barges survived. The death toll of the two fishing boats that sank together was also more than ten. In total, there were about 30 people. Kuai Xianfa, the second mate who was rescued in critical condition, suffered serious head injuries from the explosion. Peng, the section chief of the arsenal's General Affairs Section, sent him to Shanghai Hospital for treatment by car. It is said that his injuries are serious, and his life may be in danger.

Severe Alert When the disaster occurred, the military, naval, and police agencies in this port were alerted and declared martial law. They sent personnel to investigate in all directions. The Naval Guard Battalion in Gaochang Temple, because the area was most important, declared martial law and placed sentries around the wharf to prevent any accidents. After the report confirmed that the explosives had exploded, fearing that troublemakers would take the opportunity to cause trouble, the alert was not reduced. The army stationed near Gaochang Temple prohibited pedestrians from passing through.

Aftermath Arrangements Yesterday was a Sunday, and most of the arsenal staff were not at the arsenal. According to Peng, the section chief of the arsenal's General Affairs Section, the aftermath of this incident cannot be determined for the time being because the director is in Beijing. However, the arsenal will still handle the compensation for the workers who died on duty in accordance with the usual practice. Currently, they are trying to salvage the bodies. The Songhu Garrison Headquarters reported to the Ministry of Military Affairs last night after receiving confirmation.

Japanese Aircraft Carrier Arrived in Shanghai Yesterday 78

Large Quantities of Military Equipment Transported

Marines Also Landed

The Japanese Ministry of the Navy dispatched a large number of naval fleets from the Wu Naval Port to Shanghai, as reported in yesterday's newspaper. It is now learned that in addition to the cruiser "Oi" leading four destroyers of the 15th Squadron to Shanghai, an aircraft carrier and a squadron of aircraft have arrived. The information obtained is recorded separately as follows:

Warships Berth at the Wharf The four destroyers of the 15th Squadron that arrived in Shanghai the day before yesterday, "Hagi," "Fuji," "Kuzu," and "Susuki," have now been moved to the Osaka Shosen Kaisha Wharf in Yangshupu. Each ship has about 30 officers and soldiers. This time, a large amount of military equipment was transported to Shanghai for the use of the Japanese Marine Corps in Shanghai.

Military Equipment Unloaded Ashore This time, the Japanese fleet opened Shanghai. The Japanese Ministry of the Navy specially transported a large number of military goods, wartime supplies, and equipment, as well as guns, ammunition, and other items. Yesterday, they were unloaded from the "Oi" and other ships and transported ashore, including military tents for troops to camp in, building materials for trenches, military telephones, hardware, and a large number of electric nets. In addition, about three tons of new-style field guns, machine guns, shells, machine gun bullets, and fire bombs were loaded and transported ashore and stored in the Shanghai Japanese Naval Headquarters.

Marines Landed Five hundred marines were transported to Shanghai on the "Oi." Yesterday, dozens of large truckloads of goods were used to land at the Huishan Wharf. Two hundred and seventy of them were stationed at the Gongda Yarn Factory, and the rest were stationed at the Japanese barracks in Yangshupu.

Aircraft Carrier Arrived in Shanghai The aircraft carrier "Notoro," which was transferred from Lushun and carried a squadron of aircraft, arrived in Shanghai urgently yesterday at noon. It first arrived at the Wusongkou and was ordered to anchor in the third-fourth and third-fifth river tubes in the Huangpu River.

Finance Minister Huang and Others Discussed the Organization of the Financial Committee in Shanghai Yesterday 79

He Qigong to Be Appointed Secretary-General of the Financial Committee

The Standing Committee and Secretariat to Be Established in Shanghai

Banking Industry Does Not Have Such a Huge Amount of Funds Available for Advance Payments at This Time

Since Finance Minister Huang Hanliang returned to Shanghai after reinstatement, he has been actively working on the organization of the Financial Committee, in addition to requesting advance payments from the banking industry for the government's military and administrative expenses, which was discussed once a few days ago. Yesterday was Sunday, and the committee members had a lot of free time, so he specially convened a conversation meeting at Mr. Gu's private residence on Pingyuan Road, inviting Vice Minister Lin Kanghou and several members of the Financial Committee to discuss everything. It was decided that the Standing Committee and the Secretariat would be established in Shanghai, and He Qigong would be appointed Secretary-General. As for the issue of advance payments from the banking industry to the government, six financial institutions, including China Communications Bank, will be responsible for 16 million yuan. It is learned that the banking industry does not have such a huge amount of funds available at this time. The Exchange was responsible for 1 million yuan, but the reply has been received, and it can only take 500,000 yuan. The other agencies have not yet given a formal reply. The news from yesterday is recorded separately below:

Yesterday's Conversation Meeting Finance Minister Huang Hanliang convened a conversation meeting at his private residence on Pingyuan Road at 11:00 AM yesterday, inviting Vice Minister Lin Kanghou, Financial Committee members Zhang Gongquan, Chen Guangfu, Xu Jilu, and Li Fusun, among others, to discuss for two hours until about 1:00 PM. As a result, it was decided to first organize the Standing Committee and the Secretariat, which will be established in Shanghai together with the Standing Committee, and officially established in the shortest possible time. However, the inauguration ceremony will be held in Nanjing, and it was internally decided that He Qigong will be the Secretary-General of the Secretariat.

Banking Industry Advance Payments Although there was no discussion on the issue of bank advance payments yesterday, it is learned that the banking industry believes that it does not have the capacity to provide the huge amount of 16 million yuan for two-month advance payments, with the Bank of China, the Bank of Communications, and the Central Bank each responsible for 4 million yuan, the Shanghai Commercial Bank responsible for 2 million yuan, and the Exchange and the Money Shop Association each responsible for 1 million yuan. According to Financial Vice Minister Lin Kanghou, the banking industry is not sure that it can raise 7.5 million to 8 million yuan. The Exchange was originally asked to be responsible for 1 million yuan, but the reply has been received, and it can only take 500,000 yuan. The number that other financial institutions are asked to share has not yet been answered, so it is difficult to predict how much the Shanghai banking industry can raise at this time. If it is said that 5 million yuan can be raised, then it can be said with certainty. As for the fact that the Haiguan Mei, the Chief of Customs, can raise about 3 million yuan, I (Lin himself) do not know the details, he said.

Establishment of the National Postal Workers' Federation 90

Declaration Issued

The declaration of the National Postal Workers' Federation states: The National Postal Workers' Federation, which we have always remembered, has been fighting for three years through the efforts of postal workers across the country in a difficult and arduous environment, and today it can finally meet the people of the country. We are unconsciously happy and singing and dancing. We recall the struggles and experiences of the past three years, and we pursue the future of our efforts. We cannot help but feel how lovable and precious the organization born out of this difficulty and hardship is, but at the same time, we cannot help but feel how this nascent organization will work hard to break through the layers of thorns in this harsh environment. At a time when external troubles and internal strife are intertwined, especially since the "September 18th" Incident, the people of the whole country have been immersed in a feeling of sorrow and grief, wanting to use the strength of the entire nation to solve all the current difficulties. We believe that the first thing the people should do now is to automatically organize themselves, connect the various scattered forces, and transform them into an organized and united force to fight against all evil forces and imperialists. Only in this way can we relieve our suffering, and only in this way is there a way out for the entire country and the entire nation. All of us postal workers deeply feel this point, so we have gathered postal worker organizations from various places into a general federation. On the one hand, we feel that our strength has increased, and at the same time, we also acknowledge that the responsibility we bear for the country and society has increased. Here, we must put forward the mission of this federation to announce to the country, the people, and the masses that groups and politics are fundamentally inseparable. We not only passively recognize this point, but also actively assist the government to enrich this understanding. Why is Chinese politics not yet on the right track? Why have the excessive taxes and miscellaneous levies of the warlord governments over the years not aroused the resentment of the people? Why are there still intermittent civil wars in the country? Finally, why do the various imperialists openly and covertly plunder and turn China into a semi-colonial country? Why do the Chinese people have no way to abolish the unequal treaties? We dare to boldly say that everything that is contrary to the interests of the people exists because the people are not organized, have no power, and cannot assist the government. To implement the unity of the people and jointly face the national crisis, this is the reason for the establishment of this federation. 1. The postal service is one of the transportation industries, bearing the great mission of promoting culture and developing the national economy, and it is fundamentally not a profit-making organization. In recent years, due to the further corruption of internal affairs, speculators have occupied important positions in the postal service, and instead of doing what should be done from the perspective of the postal service's mission, they only know how to facilitate private interests, and they do not hesitate to break the postal service examination system in order to place relatives and old acquaintances, and turn the postal service into a commercial behavior, competing for profits with ordinary merchants. The Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau, established the year before last, is a very clear example. We postal workers now further understand that only through our own efforts can we achieve the true mission of the postal service. We advocate that the postal economy should be absolutely open and independent, and that the postal economy should prioritize the development of postal services and the expansion of postal lines. However, the scattered forces of postal workers cannot correct the erroneous policies of the authorities. Only when postal workers unite and make organized efforts can they break the current harsh environment and truly bear the fundamental mission of the postal service. To urge the postal authorities to maintain the independence of the postal economy and strive to develop postal services, this is the reason for the establishment of this federation. 2. At this representative meeting of the federation, although there were representatives from as many as sixteen provinces and regions, there were still many remote areas that were unable to send representatives due to the fact that the entire organization had not yet been established or due to environmental reasons. This is the most regrettable thing that the federation felt at this meeting. We know that the reason why remote provinces and regions that have not yet been organized or have already been organized but are not sound is not due to a lack of revolutionary spirit among the workers, but because of the small number of people and insufficient organizational strength. The comrades in remote areas must need the entire organization more urgently than the areas that have already been organized. Now that the federation organization has been established, we believe that under the leadership of this federation, all areas that have not yet been organized or have only unsound organizations will be able to organize and improve themselves, so that the overall organization will be more powerful, and at the same time, the scattered organizations will also be guaranteed. To promote local association affairs and realize the unity of postal workers across the country, this is the reason for the establishment of this federation. 3. In the riddled Chinese society, there is naturally no social organization that can be said to be perfect. Only the postal service can be considered a leader in state-owned public utilities. In fact, to recognize that the reason why the postal service has achieved this better result is entirely due to the public service, law-abiding, hard-working, and diligent work of our postal personnel. However, now the postal authorities are exploiting the vested interests of postal workers on the one hand, and on the other hand, they are actually using the surplus earned through the efforts of our postal workers to flatter others, resulting in the postal economy being on the verge of bankruptcy due to continuous destruction. Now the postal bureau has ordered all postal districts to implement austerity policies due to economic difficulties. Under this current situation, the treatment of postal workers is of course even more out of the question to improve. It must be known that all expenditures in postal construction are purely necessary to promote postal services. The current austerity policy is tantamount to a suicide policy. If the postal authorities continue to want to use the funds for postal construction and the funds for improving the treatment of workers to enrich themselves, we will inevitably oppose them strongly. But without the overall organizational strength, how can we restrain the ambitions of the authorities? To safeguard the postal service in order to improve the treatment of workers, this is the reason for the establishment of this federation. 4. Finally, we must say a few more words. Although the postal workers under the leadership of this federation are sufficient to represent all of the postal workers in the country, there are other parts of the postal workers who are under the leadership of friendly associations. We hope that in the near future, after the overall organization of the friendly association is established, it will be able to join hands with us and fight together. We believe that under joint efforts, the above four goals will inevitably be more thoroughly implemented and more guaranteed. This is the greatest wish of this federation in celebrating its establishment. Furthermore, the postal bureau is a state-owned public utility, and the only purpose of people serving in the postal service is to serve the society and strive to facilitate communication and transportation for the people. Therefore, it can be said that the postal service is not only the postal service of the country, but is actually the postal service of the entire society. Therefore, the prosperity and decline of the postal service is closely related to the interests of the people of the country. At the beginning of the establishment of this federation, we are willing to permanently uphold the above mission, work hard for the people, and hope that compatriots across the country will give us sympathetic assistance. This is the declaration. The National Postal Workers' Federation of the Republic of China, January 24, 21st year of the Republic.

Today, a petition will be submitted to the Jianghai Customs and the Supervisory Office.

More than 200 customs brokerage firms in this city are vehemently opposed to the Customs' promulgation of management regulations, which require strict registration by the fourth of this month, due to the urgency of the timeframe. In addition to dispatching representatives to Beijing to petition, they will also unite with customs brokers nationwide to strive for their cause. Yesterday afternoon at 3:00 PM, the Association of Customs Brokers convened an executive committee meeting at its clubhouse at 38 Edward Road to discuss how to respond to the Customs' deadline for registration and implementation of the management regulations. Three points were resolved: (1) Appoint Shi Zhikun, Xu Youren, Zheng Renye, and others as petition representatives, who will first petition the Jianghai Customs Supervisory Office in succession this morning. (2) If no results are achieved, the original representatives will proceed to Beijing to petition the Ministry of Finance. (3) Unite with customs brokers nationwide to resolutely oppose these three points. In addition to telegrams from customs brokers in various regions expressing their unanimous support, Xu Qingyun, a representative specially dispatched by the Hankou customs brokers, came to Shanghai to liaise closely and attended the meeting. The contents of the telegrams from various regions are recorded as follows: (1) Telegram from Changsha (excerpt): "The Ministry of Finance has issued new regulations for suppression, and our association has resolved to protest and has submitted them to party and government organs, requesting the Ministry to retract the order. Does the white three-part form still need to be affixed with a stamp, and how should it be affixed? We hope you will provide a reply for our reference. We believe that your association is located in the commercial center of the country and is a leader for customs brokers in various ports. The Jiujiang Association of Customs Brokers bows respectfully. Please reply by telegram immediately for our reference." The Shantou Transportation and Docking Department bows respectfully.

Anhui Association Helps a Distressed Young Widow 101

Ni Yang Zhenhua, a woman from Huaining County, Anhui Province, is currently 24 years old. Her father, Yang Shouzhi, worked in the Railway Bureau in Wuhu before his death at the age of 54. Her mother died early. She then married Ni Kaiyu, son of Ni Jiacai, a native of Anhui who ran the Yiwen Pavilion paper shop in Wanyuan. After the marriage, her father-in-law also died, and the shop was managed by her husband. On September 11, 1927, her husband left home in a fit of anger due to family matters, and the shop was closed. Her aunt also died of illness, and there were no uncles or brothers on either her mother's or father's side. She only has a five-year-old daughter. Destitute and helpless, with no means of support, she came to Shanghai last October to look for her husband but found no trace of him. She got lost on the way and was sent by the police to the China Relief Association for Women and Children, where she has been staying for over a year. The association noted that Yang was anxious to return home, but Anqing was far away, and she was a woman, so they sent a letter to the Anhui Association of Compatriots in Shanghai requesting that she be sent back to her hometown, which would be more appropriate. The association sent personnel to investigate and confirmed the situation. The Relief Association for Women and Children sent Yang and her daughter to the association. The association inquired about her background and address in detail. Because she was eager to return to her hometown but had no reliable companion, a member of the association, feeling sorry for her plight, temporarily housed her in his home, employed her for housework, and waited for her relatives to claim her.
