Page 11

Local News Two

Second Major Fire at Qichang Warehouse in Pudong 105

Warehouse Number Seven Completely Destroyed

The Losses from the Fire Exceed Millions

The Qichang Warehouse, managed by the British firm Jardine Matheson, is located on the opposite bank of the Huangpu River from the Wayside Wharf in Yangshupu, divided into east and west warehouses, both occupying a very wide area. On December 25 of last year, the west warehouse was carelessly set on fire, burning more than 5,000 bales of cotton. The H warehouse, built with steel frames and iron plates, was also completely destroyed, making it a rare major fire in Shanghai last year. Unexpectedly, one month later, while the embers of the west warehouse had not yet been extinguished, the east warehouse caught fire last night, starting around 7:30 PM and burning late into the night without being completely extinguished. The losses are no less than those of the west warehouse. The goods burned were also mostly cotton. The details are as follows:

Night Work Stacking Goods: The "Japanese Prince" arrived at the Qichang East Warehouse yesterday morning and docked to unload cargo. Yesterday was Sunday, which is usually a day of rest, but because the cargo on the ship needed to be unloaded quickly, the ship worked both during the day and at night, unloading the cargo from the ship and stacking it in warehouse number seven. The cargo included items such as beeswax and cigarette paper. The cargo had not yet been completely unloaded when the fire started.

Sudden Fire: Around 7:30 PM yesterday, night work had already begun, and the workers were busy stacking and unloading goods when they suddenly heard an explosion and a strange noise in warehouse number seven. Smoke quickly filled the air, and flames spread in all directions. The workers immediately retreated from the warehouse, but the disaster had already begun. Thick smoke billowed, making it difficult to breathe. In a short time, the fire broke out and spread until the entire warehouse number seven was engulfed in flames and could not be extinguished.

Entire Warehouse Burned: After the fire started, the warehouse's own fire-fighting boat immediately drew water from the Huangpu River to put out the fire. After a while, the alarm sounded, and the Customs' fire-fighting boat, the Muddy Water Ferry fire truck, and the Shanghai Municipal Council Fire Brigade boat all arrived at the scene to put out the fire. However, in addition to the newly arrived beeswax and tobacco leaves, the warehouse also contained more than 1,100 bales of cotton. After the fire started, the beeswax melted and ignited everything it touched, and the cotton fueled the blaze, making it even more intense. Although the firefighters tried their best to put out the fire, it was initially ineffective. It was not until two hours later that the fire gradually came under control, but the roof had been completely burned, leaving only the surrounding broken walls.

Extreme Danger: The ill-fated warehouse number seven was located between warehouse numbers six and nine. Warehouse number six contained mostly kerosene, and the two warehouses were very close to each other. Therefore, after warehouse number seven caught fire, warehouse number six was in imminent danger. If it were to be caught by the flames, it would be certain to be destroyed. The explosion of oil would be extremely dangerous. Fortunately, the firefighters tried their best to isolate the flames, so a major disaster was averted.

Embers of the West Warehouse: The fire at the west warehouse on December 25 was about a month before yesterday's fire at the east warehouse. Because the west warehouse contained a large amount of cotton, the embers had not been extinguished for a month, and there was always a risk of rekindling. Therefore, the warehouse constantly assigned people to guard it in preparation for putting out the fire at any time. Unexpectedly, while the embers of the west warehouse had not been extinguished, the east warehouse suddenly caught fire again. Warehouse number seven, which suffered the disaster yesterday, had been built for a long time and was not constructed with steel frames and concrete like the west warehouse. Therefore, the roof was burned very quickly after the fire started, and the flames soared into the sky, visible from the Bund in western Shanghai. The cotton, beeswax, tobacco leaves, wood, sealing wax, and oil stored in the warehouse were mostly insured, and the losses were enormous. The exact amount is unknown, but it is said that the cotton alone was worth hundreds of thousands of yuan. Added to the other goods, the scale of the losses is imaginable.

Austrian Dies After Mistakenly Entering a Martial Law Zone 106

The current foreign manager of the American Express Bank Co., Ltd. at 15 Jiujiang Road, Austrian A. Porges, lived with his wife in room 912 of the thirteen-story Western-style boarding house at the far west end of Route Petain in the French Concession. Every Saturday and Sunday, Porges would regularly take his wife for a drive in the western suburbs of Shanghai, regardless of the weather. Yesterday, he again accompanied his wife in his own car, number 7895, heading straight for the western suburbs of Shanghai. At 12:15 PM, the car arrived near Zhongshan Road on Hongqiao Road, not far from the airport. The area around the airport has always been a martial law zone, and no one, regardless of whether they are Chinese or foreign, is allowed to pass without a special pass. Porges did not pay attention and drove the car into the restricted area at high speed. The soldiers guarding the area saw the car driving past and rushed forward to stop it. Porges ignored them and continued driving straight ahead. The soldiers immediately fired a warning shot into the air, but the car continued to speed forward. The soldiers were unable to order the car to stop. In a desperate situation, they raised their guns and fired a shot at the car. The bullet entered from the rear of the car, hitting Porges in the back and piercing his chest. The car then stopped slowly. When the soldiers rushed up to check, Porges had already fallen into the car with a hole in his chest. Porges' wife was also dumbfounded. The soldiers immediately rushed to report to the airport and sent personnel to investigate. At that time, Porges had already lost consciousness and was taken to the hospital, but he died on the way. His body has now been transported to the International Funeral Home on Jiaozhou Road to await the encoffinment.

Shen Xiqing Reappointed as President of the District Court 107

Shen Bingqian, President of the Shanghai District Court, has been transferred to the position of President of the Wuhu District Court due to wartime duties. The position of President of the Shanghai Court will now be taken over by Shen Xiqing, a staff member of the Ministry of Justice. The transfer order was forwarded by the High Court yesterday. The court is currently rushing to complete the handover procedures, so the various divisions and accounting and general affairs departments are extremely busy, waiting for the new incumbent to take over. The former President Shen Xiqing is from Shaoxing and has served as the Presiding Judge of the Jiangsu High Court and the President of the Wuxian Local Court. After Mei Yigui fled, he was transferred to the position of President of the Shanghai Local Court. He resigned after the Party army recovered Shanghai in 1927. He then moved to the Presiding Judge of the Zhejiang High Court. The year before last, he was transferred to the position of Chief Clerk of the Shandong High Court. Last year, he was transferred to the position of staff member of the Ministry of Judicial Administration. This time, he is reappointed to his current position.

Achievements of the Port Quarantine Station 108

Wu Liande Hosts Banquet for Chinese and Foreign Shipping Companies

Dr. Wu Liande, Director of the Port Quarantine Station, hosted a banquet for managers and captains of Chinese and foreign shipping companies at the East Asia Restaurant on the evening of the 22nd. The banquet was scientific and full of interest, and nearly a hundred guests attended, making it a grand occasion. In his speech, he said, "Recalling December 9 of last year, I had the pleasure of meeting you all at the old Carlton Hotel. Today, I invite you to enjoy Chinese cuisine to change your palate, as Chinese cuisine also has its own merits. I would like to express my infinite wishes to you all, because port quarantine is not a matter for one family or one country. Its purpose is to protect the health of mankind and has a close relationship with international health. Although our office has not been in charge for very long, we have received a great deal of assistance from you all. Now, I am adopting the only new method of port quarantine in the world, which will not cause any inconvenience to either the passengers or the shipping companies, but will not be perfunctory. The current port quarantine system is based on the principles of the 1926 International Health Conference and is based on the implementation of quarantine work by the health authorities of various countries, and also takes into account the operations of shipping companies. Therefore, our office is also very willing to work hand in hand with you to promote the development of the health of mankind. I also hope that you will not misunderstand if you are sometimes fined for violating regulations. You must know that we have a fundamental cooperative significance for humanitarian health. I believe that you all understand this deeply. Over the years, we have received a great deal of assistance from various companies, as well as the Inspector General of Customs, the Customs Commissioner, the Shipping Department, and the Water Patrol. I would like to express my sincere gratitude. Now, I will briefly report the number of ships and crew members inspected by the medical officers of our office from October 1920 to December 1921. A total of 2,234 ships were inspected, with a tonnage of 15,142,733 tons. In Wusongkou, 697 ships were inspected, with a tonnage of 2,924,844 tons. In Shanghai, 5,414 Chinese passengers and 88,620 foreign passengers were inspected. In Wusong, 52,748 Chinese passengers and 3,514 foreign passengers were inspected. In Shanghai, 52,690 Chinese sailors, 85,309 European sailors, 72,346 Japanese sailors, and 9,705 Indian sailors were inspected. In Wusong, 39,669 Chinese sailors and 22,150 European sailors were inspected. This number does not include inland river vessels, because these vessels are exempt from quarantine during non-epidemic periods. This further illustrates the commercial development of Shanghai and the Yangtze River. I will now compare the tonnage of ships entering and leaving the Port of London in 1920: 160,085 ocean-going vessels (including cruise ships and fishing boats), totaling 22,582,014 tons, and 11,952 coastal vessels, totaling 6,650,900 tons. In 1921, the number of ships was 795, with a registered tonnage of 2,030,675 tons. 1,077 sailboats were inspected in Wusong, 1,828 in Nanshi, 401 in Yangshupu, 276 in the upper reaches of the Suzhou River, and 1,554 in the lower reaches. In total, 5,236 sailboats were inspected and disinfected this year. This is a record that can be used as a basis. In addition to quarantine and fumigation and disinfection, our office, led by myself and specialized personnel who have just returned from overseas investigations, is studying the rats and rat-related matters in the Shanghai port area. This research work will be gradually promoted to all ports in the country, so that in-depth scientific research can be conducted and benefit mankind. In addition, free treatment is provided at the attached clinics in Wusong and Nanshi for sailors in the port. Last summer, when cholera was prevalent in Shanghai, it was quickly extinguished thanks to the assistance of the health authorities of Shanghai and the concessions. A total of 482 cases of cholera were discovered, with only 57 deaths. The prevention and control work was carried out for 76 days from the start of the epidemic. After that, our office continued to carry out smallpox prevention work. Since winter, nearly one million people have been vaccinated against smallpox. We also paid special attention to ships coming from the Xiamen epidemic area and have gradually seen the extinction of the epidemic. Since January 1921, when our office took over the quarantine affairs of Xiamen Port and established an office, we have greatly renovated it and built a contagious disease hospital, which is deeply gratifying as it meets the needs of the smallpox epidemic in Xiamen. When our office took over, there were only two quarantine boats and one fumigation and disinfection boat. Now, we have expanded to four large boats and two disinfection boats. This is also a small achievement that I have striven to build for the country. I deeply hope that within the shortest possible time, we can develop more than 100 important ports along the coast and inland rivers of the country equally, so that we can keep pace with all advanced countries. In order to ensure the swift reception of world epidemic information, our office has established a secret telegraph code with the Far East Health Bureau stationed in Singapore by the League of Nations and the port quarantine agencies of major countries to exchange information and facilitate quarantine. Today, I have presented the duties and plans of our office to you all, and I deeply hope to exchange knowledge to correct any shortcomings and solemnly express my gratitude for your past assistance and my hope for your guidance in the future. I offer a cup of water and wine to wish the representatives of all major shipping companies good health.

National Medicine Industry Opposes Elevated Cost of Cortex Moutan 109

The Municipal National Medicine Industry Association convened an urgent meeting the other day to address the inflated market price of Cortex Moutan by pharmaceutical companies. Attendees included executive committee members Li Kangnian, Zhou Qiansheng, Zhou Zhide, Zhang Hongzhao, Sun Wen'an, Zhuang Meitang, Niu Hegao, Feng Jinpu, Guo Baosheng, Zhang Meian, and Guangfu, among others. Zhuang Meitang chaired the meeting. Zhang Hongzhao, who proposed the meeting, reported on the situation where four firms – Yongtai Fu, Heli Yuan, Yicheng, and Licheng – had exclusive sales rights for Cortex Moutan, monopolizing the market. After discussion, it was unanimously decided to firmly oppose the monopolistic behavior of Yongtai Fu and others. Besides instructing all members to slow down the processing of Cortex Moutan raw materials in preparation for returning them to the sellers, a letter of protest was sent to the Pharmaceutical Industry Association, demanding a response within three days. The letter stated that the market price of Cortex Moutan should be based on the Hangzhou market price and not exceed it; otherwise, the goods would be returned to show determination. The letter reads as follows:

To the Pharmaceutical Industry Association,

We are writing to inform you that the four companies, Yongtai Fu, Yicheng, Licheng, and Heli Yuan, in your industry have for years monopolized the sale of Cortex Moutan, arbitrarily raising wholesale prices and using purely capitalistic means to manipulate the market. This oppresses small and medium-sized merchants and indirectly increases the burden on poor and sick families, which greatly affects society and commerce. Our association believes that the purpose of an industry association is to correct the malpractices of its members. Your association, as the leader of the pharmaceutical industry, has remained silent on the monopolistic behavior and market manipulation of Yongtai Fu and others, which is deeply perplexing. This year, the opening price of Cortex Moutan has risen to a staggering 150 taels of silver per dan (unit of weight), more than double the 70-80 taels per dan it sold for three years ago. However, the opening price in Hangzhou is only 200 yuan per dan, with an 80% weight conversion. Given that Shanghai and Hangzhou are neighboring cities with the same goods from the same sources, such a significant difference is hardly fair. Moreover, with Western medicine increasingly encroaching upon the market share of traditional Chinese medicine, the monopolistic behavior only gives the Western medical community more ammunition for criticism. The members of our association have suffered under this oppression for years and refuse to be treated like mere commodities any longer. We convened an urgent meeting today and unanimously decided to firmly oppose the monopolistic behavior of Yongtai Fu and others in manipulating the Cortex Moutan market. We have also resolved that the market price of Cortex Moutan in this city should be based on the Hangzhou market price and not exceed it, aiming to stabilize prices and alleviate the burden on the poor and sick. If Yongtai Fu and others insist on pursuing their monopolistic agenda and disregard public opinion, our members will have no choice but to return the goods to show our determination. We request that your association respond within three days of receiving this letter so that we may take further action.

Sincerely,

Grand Performance of Martial Arts by Postal Workers 110

The Shanghai Postal Workers' Union Martial Arts Division held its first public performance yesterday to promote the martial spirit. More than fifty members of the division attended, along with over three hundred guests, including Tong Zhongyi, Yao Fuchun, Ding Baoyuan, Wang Zhenzhang, Zhang Pinsan, and Xia Zigang. The Postal Workers' Volunteer Army and Boy Scouts maintained order at the venue. The performance began at 2:00 PM. Members Wang Yaojian, Zhang Guangzhi, Ma Tengyun, Ni Tingfu, Wang Shunchang, Sun Wenjie, Rong Zhikang, Li Sanhe, Lu Shouzhen, Xu Jinsong, Zheng Jihai, and others successively performed long fist, demonstrating seasoned skills and delivering exceptional performances. Teacher Li Chunting's Tai Chi Chuan received high praise from the audience. Members Zhang Kejing's Fenmen Thirteen Swords, Sun Wenjie's Bagua Double Sabers, Yao Qiuhua's Twelve-Series Spears, Li Yu's Night Battle Five Marquis Saber, Ni Tingfu's Swallow Wing Shield, and Li Tinghai's Pilgrim Staff were all exceptionally skilled and flawless. In particular, Coach Li's Bagua Tiger Head Hook, rarely seen in Shanghai, was a highlight. Paired performances included White Monkey vs. Golden Rooster, Double Axes Breaking Spear, Double Hands Replacing Spear, Single Saber Breaking Flower Spear, Two-Headed Snake Breaking Double Spear, Double Blade Deflecting Saber, Sha Zi Staff Breaking Spear, and Three-Section Staff Breaking Spear. The variety of performances was dazzling and captivating. Later, guest and wrestling master Tong Zhongyi performed Huagong Fist and Eight Immortals Sword, and then wrestled with Wang Zhenzhang, earning thunderous applause and admiration. Yao Fuchun's Xingyi Quan and Three Talents Sword were also highly praised by the guests. Zhang Pinsan's Taiyi Drunken Fist, Ding Baoyuan's Spring and Autumn Broadsword, Wang Zhenzhang's Liuhe Spear, and Xia Zigang's Bagua Hook were all performed with great effort. The event concluded with a group photo and dismissal.

Electrical and Silk Weaving Industry Association Petitions for Investigation into Similar Organization 112

The Shanghai Electrical and Silk Weaving Industry Association submitted a petition to the Municipal Party Headquarters and the Social Affairs Bureau yesterday, stating that it had discovered an illegal organization forming without authorization, and requested a thorough investigation and prohibition to avoid confusion and misrepresentation. The association stated that since its establishment, it has a long history, and when public organizations were reorganized according to law, it was approved and registered by the Municipal Bureau and the Shanghai Party Headquarters, recognizing it as the legal group for the electrical and silk weaving industry in Shanghai. However, on the 22nd of this month, the association read in the *Shi Bao* newspaper that Lu Zhongying and others had initiated the establishment of the Shanghai Fine Weaving Electrical Silk Fabric Industry Association, and had convened a meeting yesterday at No. 3, Lane 3, Zhenhua Lane, Malong Road, electing Lu Zhongying and eight others as preparatory committee members. Regardless of the truth, and whether the report is entirely fictitious, Article 4 of the Implementing Rules for Industry Associations stipulates that if two or more organizations are initiated in the same industry, the local competent authority shall verify and determine which is legitimate. Furthermore, the association was established earlier and registered according to law, and it is difficult to allow an illegal organization to be established afterward, as it would violate the law and hinder association affairs, which is extremely undesirable. Therefore, in addition to attaching the news report from the *Shi Bao* newspaper, the association is submitting this petition for your office to review and investigate thoroughly, to prohibit the illegal organization, to avoid confusion, and for the public benefit of industry and commerce. It is reported that the Municipal Party Headquarters and the Municipal Chamber of Commerce have also submitted similar petitions.

Boatman's Fiancee Transforms into a Modern Woman After Coming to Shanghai 114

Living a Romantic Life in the Dance Hall

Unwilling to Marry the Boatman

The dancer Wu Ailin, originally named Hou Panying, also known as Gendi, was betrothed to Genquan by her parents when she was fifteen years old. Shortly after, her father passed away, and her mother was unable to support her, so she was raised in her husband's family. However, the following year, Genquan's parents also passed away one after another. Genquan, needing to inherit his father's business, went out to work as a boatman, and sent Ailin to live with her aunt. Unexpectedly, in May of last year, she was enticed to come to Shanghai and became a dancer in a dance hall. Due to the influence of the environment, she completely changed her ways. Her mother also regretted the marriage and hired a lawyer to publish a notice in the newspaper stating that her daughter had never been betrothed to anyone. Genquan, upon reading the newspaper, rushed to his aunt's house to inquire, only to find that Ailin had long left. He immediately came to Shanghai and filed a petition with the First Special District Court, requesting mediation. However, Wu Ailin consistently avoided appearing, ultimately leading to the failure of mediation. Now, Wu Genquan has formally filed a lawsuit, requesting that their marriage contract be confirmed as legal. However, Ailin has now transformed into a purely modern young woman, showing no trace of her former village girl appearance. Having seen and heard nothing but extravagance, she is unwilling to marry a boatman. The matter is quite clear. Judge Yang held a hearing the other day and ordered a continued hearing at a later date to investigate the evidence.

Tan Meiying Files for Divorce for the Second Time 115

Zhao Guangzu's Nature Remains Unchanged

Living with a Dancer Again

Zhao Guangzu, residing at No. 60, Jingxin Lane, Huade Road, is a young and romantic man who particularly enjoys frequenting brothels. Several years ago, he was swindled out of the property deed of his house by the courtesan Mei Fei and Hu San, who mortgaged it away. His wife, Tan Meiying, was angered by this and turned against him, first suing Mei Fei for fraud in court, and then filing for divorce from Zhao. After the initial trial ruled against her, Mei Fei, unwilling to accept the verdict, filed an appeal against Tan Meiying. Tan Meiying also appealed the initial ruling against her divorce. Later, with the intervention of friends and relatives from all sides, both cases were settled peacefully. From then on, Mei Fei remained a goddess, and Zhao and Tan reconciled. After such a dramatic turn of events, it was believed that Zhao would stay away from the stages and dance halls and live with Tan until their hair turned white. Unexpectedly, the separation began again after only a year of reconciliation. Tan has now hired lawyer Jiang Yiping to request that the First Special District Court's civil mediation office summon Zhao Guangzu to court for divorce mediation. According to her statement, shortly after their reconciliation, Zhao relapsed into his old habits, abandoning his proper business and neglecting his family. He is now involved with the dancer Wang Aliu from the Dahu Dance Hall, openly cohabiting with her at No. 12, Xiangkang Lane, Baike Road. On the 2nd of this month, the plaintiff personally witnessed the two sleeping together. He spends his time gambling and wandering outside, often not returning home for several days. The debts he owes are constantly being demanded by creditors at the door, leaving her unable to cope. Recently, when she asked him for household expenses, he became enraged and assaulted her, showing no kindness or gratitude. Although he owns assets worth 100,000 yuan, he spends them recklessly, giving her whatever she demands. If all the family property is squandered one day, how will the plaintiff survive? Therefore, she requests mediation to persuade them to divorce and to order Zhao to pay her 20,000 yuan in alimony to support her livelihood. Judge Yang Yi held a hearing on Saturday, but because Zhao did not appear, the mediation could not proceed, and the hearing was adjourned to a later date.

Peppermint Oil Lawsuit Still Unresolved 116

Zhu Jiliang, the general manager of the Shanghai Zhenhua Peppermint Manufacturing Factory, previously sent Li Qianwan, the manager of the factory, to Ji'an, Jiangxi Province, to purchase peppermint oil. Li then entered into an agency contract with Liu Youdao of the local Gongping Store and Wang Rongzhai of the Shengji Store, setting a fixed price. The two stores then shipped 10,000 catties (unit of weight) to Shanghai. However, Zhu suddenly complained that the price was too high and delayed picking up the goods and paying. Liu and Wang had no choice but to hire lawyers Zhan Jifeng and Zhan Yigang to file a lawsuit against Zhu and Li, requesting the court to order the defendants to repay the 122,300 yuan in advance payments. The case was heard again by Judge Li of the First Special District Court the other day. Defendant Zhu Jiliang still claimed that he only instructed Li Qianwan to go to Jiangxi to purchase goods for cash and had no right to enter into a contract. He equivocated in every possible way. Judge Li, understanding the defendant's intention to overturn the contract due to the lack of profit, tried to persuade Zhu to reach a settlement with the plaintiffs. Plaintiff lawyer Zhan Jifeng stated that the plaintiffs deeply understood the court's intention to resolve the matter peacefully and were willing to settle. However, Zhu ultimately did not want to suffer any losses and shifted all the responsibility to Li Qianwan, claiming that the contract was privately entered into by Li and that he would file criminal charges against Li. The plaintiff's lawyer argued that Zhu was intentionally delaying the matter and requested that the court make a swift ruling. Judge Li then ordered the defendant to either settle the case or file a lawsuit against Li within a week; otherwise, the case would continue to be heard.

The case of lawyer Ren Zhennan being accused by Yong businessman Zhuang Chunfu of defrauding him of money has been ruled in First Instance by the Shanghai District Court. Reader Communication

Please, Gentlemen, Scatter Wealth to Aid the Distressed 123

Hong Nian

The current crises facing China are: (1) The lack of "sincere unity" among key party and government figures creates political instability; (2) Japan's occupation of the Northeast stirs up public unrest; (3) Victims of disasters (including disaster areas, war zones, and bandit areas) and refugees (referring to those fleeing the Northeast and those under Japanese rule) have no means of support and will resort to desperate measures; (4) The Red Army and the Communist Party advocate violent revolution to disrupt social order; (5) Thus creating a state of internal and external pressure on today's situation. How can this situation be "rectified" and "saved"? Clearly, it is necessary to quell internal troubles on one hand and resist foreign aggression on the other. But regardless of internal or external matters, the most important thing is to solve the economic problem first. We see that the disaster relief for floods, the relief for refugees in the Northeast, the assistance to Ma Zhanshan, and the support for the Volunteers in recent months have all been based on public donations. This "donation" is the quick fix for both internal and external problems. Examining the contributors to each donation, most are ordinary people with conscience and good intentions, especially ordinary people and poor vendors and paupers. They sympathize with the compatriots in distress and the patriotic soldiers, donating their lifelong savings with hard work and effort. How admirable and touching is this! What about the high-ranking officials? We rarely hear of them donating a single penny. Are they all "incorruptible and impoverished," poorer than even the vendors and paupers? I don't believe it, I don't believe it. After reading the previous newspaper statistics comparing the private wealth of certain officials to several million, I believe it even less. The government is as poor as the Beijing government, and even government agencies and offices are facing "starvation" and closure. At the same time, we also hear that many high-ranking officials deposit their money in foreign banks, remit money to foreign countries to buy land, operate large enterprises in the country, buy land, and build houses and villas. Therefore, I formally suggest that after those in power abandon their prejudices and establish a truly unified government, they should ask the high-ranking officials to generously donate two-thirds or one-half of their private property to save their compatriots, eliminate internal troubles, strengthen national defense, and fight foreign wars. "Distributing wealth will gather people." Distributing wealth is the best way to win over the people. If everyone has food to eat, then what Communist Red Army can stir up trouble again? Give generous rewards to brave men and store provisions for war. Diplomacy backed by military strength is bound to be victorious. This is the effective way to save the "crisis" and "disaster." (B)

Education News

Important News

Ministry of Education Statistics on National Secondary Education 125

The Ministry of Education previously issued a general order to investigate the general situation of secondary education throughout the country. However, it took a long time to verify and reply before accurate statistics could be obtained. The Ministry has, up to the 20th year (of the Republic), compiled statistics on the general situation of secondary education based on the results of previous investigations. The main points are described below: (1) There are a total of 1,339 secondary schools in the country, including one national school, 354 provincial and municipal schools, 566 county schools, and 418 private schools. (2) There are a total of 690 junior high schools, 16 senior high schools, 248 complete secondary schools, 149 vocational schools, and 236 normal schools in the country. (3) The total number of students in secondary schools in the country is 234,811, including 107,609 in junior high school, 4,080 in senior high school, 77,011 in complete secondary school, 16,641 in vocational school, and 29,470 in normal school. (4) The number of male and female students in secondary schools across the country is 192,707 and 37,604, respectively. (5) The total funding for secondary schools across the country is 24,602,366 yuan, including 8,232,611 yuan for junior high school, 5,683,332 yuan for senior high school, 10,116,711 yuan for complete secondary school, 2,217,480 yuan for vocational school, and 3,468,072 yuan for normal school. (6) The average annual cost per student in various secondary schools is 7.64 yuan for junior high school, 13.93 yuan for senior high school, 13.14 yuan for complete secondary school, 13.34 yuan for vocational school, and 11.77 yuan for normal school. (7) The average number of students taught by each teacher in various secondary schools is 13 in junior high school, 10 in senior high school, 11 in complete secondary school, 11 in vocational school, and 8 in normal school.

Summary of the Past Year's Work of the Ministry of Education 126

(Continued from yesterday)

In the summer of the 20th year [of the Republic, i.e., 1931], based on the findings of the 17th year's [1928] survey and statistics, a general overview of secondary education throughout the country was compiled, and the "Outline for Secondary Education Facilities" was promulgated. All provinces and cities were instructed to comply with it starting from the 20th year. The main points are: 1. Ordinary secondary schools in all provinces and cities are already more numerous than vocational schools, so high school ordinary courses and junior high schools will not be added for the time being. 2. All provinces should add higher and lower-level agricultural and industrial vocational schools, depending on the circumstances. 3. County secondary schools should stop enrolling ordinary secondary school students and instead enroll vocational or rural normal school students. If it is indeed necessary to establish a secondary school, a vocational course or rural normal school course should still be attached. 4. All secondary schools should uniformly add vocational subjects or attach vocational courses. 5. Vocational schools or vocational courses attached to secondary schools should raise sufficient funds, strengthen equipment, and earnestly cultivate students' labor habits and production skills. 6. If private individuals in counties and cities apply to establish ordinary secondary schools, except in cases where the county or city is too far from the provincial secondary school and it is verified that it is necessary, they may be approved for establishment at their discretion; otherwise, they should be supervised or persuaded to change to agricultural, industrial, or other vocational schools. (6) Improving elementary education, such as promulgating standards for primary schools, kindergartens, and equipment, formulating standards for primary school moral education, and reviewing textbooks for primary school children (more than one hundred have been approved and determined, more than fifty have been returned for revision, and recently a committee has been organized to formulate standards for the compilation of children's books for the elementary education section). Investigating the general situation of elementary education throughout the country and promoting compulsory education (provinces and cities that have organized compulsory education committees include Hubei, Jiangxi, Guangdong, Hebei, Henan, Anhui, Zhejiang, Jiangsu, Hunan, Shandong, Shaanxi, Gansu, and other provinces and regions. Those with plans approved for pilot implementation include Nanjing City, which promotes elementary education in stages, Shanghai City, which has designated pilot zones for compulsory education, Tianjin City, which has proposed a compulsory education implementation plan, Jiangsu Province, which has proposed preliminary measures for pilot compulsory education and is preparing to establish simplified primary schools and formulate provisional standards for simplified primary school courses, Fujian Province, which has established regulations for compulsory education pilot zones, Hubei Province, which has added municipal and rural compulsory education pilot zones and is running fifty provincial primary schools and has established an implementation plan, Sichuan Province, which has established an implementation plan, and Shandong Province, which has established a promotion plan. In April of the 20th year, two methods related to promoting compulsory education were promulgated: one is the method for enriching children's enrollment in rural primary schools, and the other is the method for promoting primary education in prosperous cities. Recently, all provinces and cities have been instructed to follow these methods and submit detailed plans for approval and implementation.) Guaranteeing local educational funds (the "Measures for the Custody of Local Educational Funds" were formulated in May of the 20th year and submitted to the Executive Yuan for an order to all provincial and municipal governments to comply). (7) Promoting social education, such as promoting mass education (according to the latest report, there are a total of 20,089 mass schools nationwide, with Hebei having the most, with 6,606 schools, followed by Shanxi, with 5,734 schools. To facilitate literacy, efforts are being made to promote the phonetic alphabet), promoting libraries (there are 1,620 libraries nationwide, including 1 national library, 48 provincial libraries, 1,052 municipal and county and private libraries, 397 libraries attached to schools, 75 libraries attached to institutions and associations, and 41 libraries with specialized characteristics), promoting the national calendar and high-minded entertainment, soliciting national anthems, collecting educational products to be transported to Belgium for exhibition (China's performance ranked third), inspecting films, and organizing a calendar research association. (8) Strictly enforcing military training. (9) Developing Mongolian and Tibetan education, such as establishing a Mongolian and Tibetan Education Department, investigating Mongolian and Tibetan education, training Mongolian and Tibetan teachers, and preparing for Mongolian and Tibetan schools in Nanjing and Kangding. Translating textbooks and important laws and regulations (End).

Jinan Lost to Lux Due to Strategic Error 133

Result: 0 to 3

The A-League Championship is Inevitably Shaken

Scott Still Leads

The Jinan team, which had hoped to win the A-League championship for Westerners, lost to Lux yesterday with a score of zero to three due to the absence of general Chen Zhenhe due to a leg injury and the lack of a commander at the front, resulting in no offensive ability. Fortunately, its internal guards were strong and able to maintain the half-wall for 75 minutes. Suddenly changing tactics, Liang Shutang was appointed as the forward, and as soon as a loophole was exposed, three goals were lost in a row. The game ended with a score of zero to three, losing to Lux. The future of the A-League championship is inevitably shaken. Spectators at the China Baseball Field were also disappointed. Referee: Maxwell.

Beaker, Archie

Chen Fuzhong, Mei Hongbao

Old Injury Recurred Shortly After the Start of the Game

Jinan played against the wind, and Qiu Zhongfeng dribbled the ball to attack. The ball went back and forth in the central area with little progress. After five minutes, Qiu's old injury recurred and he left the field to rest. Jinan's morale was shaken, and the enemy invaded and pressed on from all sides, advancing on five fronts. Chen Buzhang, Jiang Shanjing, Feng Yunyou, and Liang Shutang separately blocked them with no chance to take advantage of. After ten minutes, Qiu re-entered the game with his injury, and the situation turned to balance. Qiu's attack was weak, and the Lux goalkeeper caught the ball at will. Liang Shutang supplemented it, and Mei Hongbao shot from the ground but went into the goalkeeper's hands.

Preserving the Goal is Left to Fate

The overall situation was that Jinan's forward attack was weak, and the internal guards were naturally doubly shocked. However, the enemy was seen invading one after another, attacking repeatedly. Occasionally breaking through for a counterattack, there was nothing surprising. Liang Shutang suddenly made up his mind, acting as a lone army, and actually made a long expedition. Although he didn't hit the target, it was a slight consolation to the people. Lux's forward Becker also launched a remote attack, and Jiang Shanjing returned the block slightly obliquely. The ball trended inward, fortunately touching the wooden pillar and remaining unscathed. Escaping from the dead, the forward rose up and first forced a corner kick, followed by Mei Hongbao's pass, and finally saw Qiu Dongyan's header, hitting the goalpost. Qiu then kicked it, and the first half ended with a whistle after crossing the goal, with a score of zero to zero.

Three Goals Lost in a Row Due to Strategic Error

At the start of the second half, Jinan had a turning point, assisted by the wind, and felt even more impressive. Mei Hongbao approached the enemy's goal, but did not attack himself, letting Qiu do it. Qiu's injury had not fully healed, so how could he have strength? As a result, a great opportunity was wasted. Lux launched an attack, but it was also ineffective, resulting in a stalemate. Within thirty minutes, Jinan was safe due to its strong internal guards. Suddenly, Lux forward H. Mada fell to the ground with the ball, injured his arm and left the field, thinking it was a gift from heaven, changing their strategy and switching Liang and Fu's positions, in order to emphasize the offensive side. Unexpectedly, due to this change, Archie took the opportunity to pass the ball in front of the goal, Chen Buzhang slapped it out with both hands, and Thompson greeted it with his head, hitting the inside of the goal squarely. As the floodgates opened, the flood poured in. Archie kicked in the second goal, and Lochha scored the third goal.

Heroes Lose Their Temper When Their Nest is Overturned

When the first goal was lost, Jinan switched Feng and Zhuang again, hoping to thicken the forward strength. Who knew that the second and third goals were scored in succession. So they fully focused on the attack, hoping for a turning point. However, the players felt the pain of having their nest overturned, and actually acted barbaric, which was a miscalculation. At that time, the saying that the spirit of the Second Xia was more important than victory or defeat was probably put out of their minds. Jiang Shanjing became emotional, fouled and was sent off, and Jinan lost a line of defense as a result. However, at that time, both sides had no fighting spirit, and the game soon came to a close. Jinan lost to zero to three. From then on, Lincoln West captured an invisible ascent to a higher level in the A-League, while Scott won the Navy with four to zero yesterday, actually ranking first among the teams.

Commercial News

Financial Gold Prices Weaken Last Week After Initial Sharp Rise 139

Highest Nearly 700 Taels

Fluctuations Reached 38 Taels Throughout the Week. Gold prices last week still experienced drastic changes, with turbulent waves and unstoppable momentum. Daily differences reached over ten taels, leaving traders bewildered and at a loss. Consequently, supply and demand varied greatly. At the beginning of the week, momentum was still strong, with prices nearly reaching 700 taels. Afterward, a swirling pattern emerged until the end of the week, when the trend weakened sharply, plummeting to the 610-tael mark. The entire week saw a fluctuation of 38 taels, with a total decrease of 9 taels and 6 mace. This was mainly due to the overseas silver market first falling and then rising, resulting in a slight overall drop. The Shanghai market's exchange rate for British pounds shrank by half a notch, and the U.S. dollar exchange rate shrank by 0.875. Internal bank rates also slightly declined overall. Although British and U.S. exchange rates remained tight, the gold market moved in the opposite direction, greatly affected by the unsettled situation. Furthermore, news circulated from abroad that France had repeatedly withdrawn large sums of deposits from the U.S., and Germany intended to postpone war reparations, temporarily not making payments, all of which were unfavorable to the gold market. Consequently, hedging with exchange drafts gradually widened to over 50 taels, likely due to gold dealers colluding to create blank drafts to profit from arbitrage. This had a significant impact, pushing the settlement price of U.S. dollars from 50 taels to as high as 80 taels. For those who had not settled their two-month forward contracts for March, they initially had to pay over one tael to close the position. However, due to an oversupply of spot gold, they only needed to pay a few cents, and eventually, they even received a few cents. In the end, short positions had to pay two to three taels to close, a completely unexpected reversal. Furthermore, interest for red bar gold initially increased by ten taels, with Yufeng and Yongheng showing buying interest, but now only increased by four and a half taels. There were few consultants offering advice. The following is a summary of the week's developments:

Prices Continue to Fall by 9 Taels and 6 Mace. At the beginning of the week (January 18), Da Tiao Bank continued to shrink by 0.3125, and the silver price shrank by 0.375. The Xianling exchange rate initially shrank by 0.375, with the U.S. dollar at 0.75. Later, it was revised to a shrinkage of 0.25, with the U.S. dollar also at 0.25. Internally, Tingxiu Bank had high settlement volumes, and gold dealers were scrambling to collude. As for the gold market, it initially rose by 9 taels, reaching 688 taels, then 86 taels and 8 mace. Subsequently, due to excessive buying, it surged past 90 taels, reaching 96 taels and 8 mace. Later, large investors sold off, and the midday price was 89 and a half taels. In the afternoon, the market opened again at 93 taels, then retreated to 88 and a half taels, with selling pressure prevailing. By the close, it still trended upward, reaching 92 taels and 7 mace, a sharp increase of 13 taels and 9 mace compared to the previous Saturday. The day saw a fluctuation of 10 taels. On Tuesday, Da Tiao Bank further shrank by 0.375 to 0.3125, and the silver price shrank by 0.375. The Xianling exchange rate remained unchanged, and the internal rate remained flat. Dealers were scrambling to collude, with more covering than shorting. The gold market opened slightly higher by 8 mace, reaching 93 and a half taels. Due to unfavorable conditions and U.S. buying, news spread of a silver meeting, and prices fell from 95 taels to 92 taels. However, the exchange market tightened, reaching 99 taels. Then, with the U.S. dollar seemingly loosening, the midday price was 91 taels and 2 mace. In the afternoon, the market initially rose to 96 taels and 5 mace, then 98 taels. Due to large investors chasing purchases, Wu and others sold off, causing the price to fall back to 88 and a half taels. However, the closing price was 90 taels and 8 mace, slightly lower than the previous day by 1 tael and 9 mace, with a difference of 10 taels and 5 mace. On Wednesday, Da Tiao Bank rose by 0.125 to 0.1875, with the silver price unchanged. The local Xianling exchange rate remained unchanged, and the U.S. dollar shrank by 0.125, as the exchange rate tightened again. British and U.S. internal rates seemed to loosen, with little trading activity. The initial gold price was 92 and a half taels, an increase of 1 tael and 7 mace, as the silver price remained unchanged. However, conditions were still unfavorable, and the U.S. bought again. Soon after, prices retreated to 90 taels, but buying interest was strong, pushing the price up to 94 taels and 9 mace. However, although public bonds had opened, prices fell sharply. Furthermore, due to France withdrawing deposits from the U.S., sentiment was downward. The midday price was only 85 taels and 2 mace, and the afternoon opened at 83 and a half taels. Afterward, the market was relatively peaceful, with the closing price at 85 taels, a further drop of 5 taels and 8 mace. The entire day saw a difference of 11 taels and 4 mace. On Thursday, Da Tiao Bank slightly declined by 0.125, with the silver price unchanged. The Xianling exchange rate remained the same, and the internal British rate was flat while the U.S. rate shrank, due to exchange rate factors. However, dealers were heavily colluding. The gold market opened higher by 5 taels, reaching 89 taels, then 7 and a half taels. Later, as the exchange market strengthened, it rose to 91 taels and 9 mace. However, due to small spot transactions, large investors and banks sold off, causing the price to plummet by over 10 taels, reaching 79 taels and 8 mace. A Glimpse of the Difficulties of the Silver and Money Industry 142

Inferior Goods Sealed and Not Sold

Securities Prices Depressed

Heavy Losses from Floods

The silver and money industry faces a significant challenge every time it solicits outstanding debts at the end of the accounting period. However, the difficulties this time are even greater than in previous years. The difficulties stem from: (1) Significant losses due to the seizure of inferior goods from various shops. The silver for the goods' price must rely on money shops for turnover. Now that the goods are sealed, there is no way to obtain cash. Although the debt collection is strict, there is no recourse. (2) The securities craze. Recently, due to difficulties in extending credit, the financial community has changed course, with many purchasing securities for profit. The sharp drop in securities prices has caused significant losses for the silver and money industry, as well as harming outsiders. Therefore, it is impossible to clear outstanding debts as desired. (3) Last year's floods caused damage to various commercial cities, and many merchants outside the affected areas were left with nothing. The goods were damaged by flooding, and the debt collection was delayed. If such a chaotic situation is not resolved, the silver and money industry will be in a difficult position. Due to the above three difficulties, there is no clear direction for this round of soliciting outstanding debts. According to the industry's announcement yesterday, only one-tenth or one-twelfth of the debts have been collected. This is a difficult situation never seen before in the commercial market.

Page 13

Free Talk

A Husbandman's Talks on Not Removing Garden Weeds

An Unprecedented Advertisement 149

It's a very misguided attitude to read the newspaper without looking at the advertisements. When I unfolded the newspaper yesterday morning, I seemed to see the big characters "Renouncing the Qualification of County Magistrate" in the advertisement column. I didn't pay attention at the time, and I flipped it over to national affairs.

Although these words were neglected by my attitude of neglecting advertisements, they had somehow left a very deep impression in my subconscious. So "Renouncing the Qualification of County Magistrate" ...... "Renouncing the Qualification of County Magistrate" ...... "Renouncing the Qualification of County Magistrate" ...... floated out of my mind one after another. Finally, I suddenly came to a conclusion, "Renouncing the Qualification of County Magistrate, I'm afraid it's not an ordinary advertisement!" I reopened the newspaper and found such a headline: "Former Liyang County Magistrate Li Jinfang Declares Renunciation of Jiangsu Province's Second Session of County Magistrate Qualification".

I carefully read the content from beginning to end and extracted the following facts:

(1) Li Jinfang was dismissed from his post by Pan Keping, the director of the Finance Bureau, who was recommended by Ye Chucang, the chairman of Jiangsu Province, for reporting Pan Keping's malfeasance.

(2) After being dismissed, Li Jinfang submitted the illegal acts of the provincial government in clearing up the case to the Supervisory Yuan and the Zhenjiang District Court;

(3) The Supervisory Yuan has filed an impeachment against the principal offender in the case, and Pan Keping has also been arrested and imprisoned by the Ministry of Military and Political Affairs;

(4) The Jiangsu Province Examination Regulations clearly stipulate that the recommender should be punished if corruption is discovered in the recommended personnel, but Ye Chucang and others remained unscathed;

(5) Ye Chucang was the chief examiner of the second county magistrate examination in Jiangsu Province, so he had a teacher-student relationship with Li Jinfang. Li Jinfang followed Gu Tinglin's example of denying being a student of the traitorous official Qian Qianyi and voluntarily renounced the qualification of county magistrate and refused to receive the review diploma;

(6) Li Jinfang declared that he had obtained the qualification of county magistrate in the Hubei Political Affairs Committee, although it was useless, he was willing to keep it. If the above sections are completely true, then former county magistrate Li's statement contains important significance; the reason why this significance is important is because it contains a representative struggle - fighting out a clean county magistrate under corruption, on top of corruption, and in the midst of corruption.

Struggle is the grand avenue to building a clean government. We must be strict with ourselves and strict with our superiors in order to create a clean society.

Miao People's Customs Chronicle 150

— Zhang Yan

I recently read the Hunan Provincial Government's county administration report, which detailed the social customs of various counties. I have selected a few excerpts from the Miao customs of Yongshui County to share with readers.

Yongshui County is connected to Xiushan in Sichuan, Songtao in Guizhou, and Baojing, Fenghuang, Qiancheng, and other counties in this province. In Yongshui County, the Han and Miao people live together. In the county's upper and lower nine townships, upper and lower eight townships, upper and lower ten townships, and so on, there are fewer Han people and more Miao people. Their languages are mutually unintelligible, and they do not understand "Kehua" (Mandarin, commonly called "Kehua"). As a result, many Miao people do not understand government policies and other publicity. Currently, the government is paying special attention to education, and in addition to expanding schools, it is also ordering the learning of Kehua in order to eliminate the distinction between Han and Miao people and assimilate them.

Miao people do not believe in vaccination. They do not know about smallpox or cowpox at all. Therefore, even if someone dies from smallpox, the Miao people not only do not blame anyone but attribute it to fate and let nature take its course.

Whether in spring, summer, autumn, or winter, Miao boys and girls all wear wind caps on their heads. They do not remove them even in the hottest weather. In the severe winter, they do not remove their caps and still go barefoot. It can be said that they care for their heads but not their feet. Or is it simply a habit?

Land in Yongshui is used for military reclamation, and the economy is notoriously backward. What is used in the market and believed by the general public are mostly Sichuan copper coins worth 100 and 50 "cash," and single or double copper coins from this province are rarely seen. Even the Yuan head silver coins are often rejected by the Miao people. (Remainder omitted)

In Yongshui, the Han and Miao people live together, and their lives are extraordinarily simple. They eat two meals a day. For the Miao people, corn and sweet potatoes are the only source of nourishment. The people here are mostly accustomed to hard work. Both men and women are good at carrying things on their shoulders. Women often go barefoot and wear straw sandals, earning a living independently and not relying on men.

The Miao people in Yongshui account for seventy to eighty percent of the population. The customs and habits of the Han people are still common, but the Miao people are different. It is said that when someone dies, they only sing mourning songs and wail, and they do not usually follow the prescribed mourning clothes. When a woman marries, there is no betrothal or name asking. Only a matchmaker lights incense and sets off firecrackers as a form of engagement. Sometimes, men and women can choose their partners freely through singing to each other. Other things, such as spring social gatherings, dragon dances, New Year's dragon lanterns, lion dances, and swings, are especially lively. Although the Miao people are superstitious about ghosts and gods, they do not kneel before idols. Therefore, those who are relatively wealthy always prepare a cow in winter. They choose a date, tie it to a pillar, and stab it with spears. This is called "Chuiniu Jigui" (stabbing the cow to sacrifice to ghosts), also known as "Huan Nuoyuan" (returning the exorcism vow).

When Miao women give birth, they can also drink cold water without any danger. A Miao woman must marry several husbands before she dies. Marriage is not taken very seriously. In funerals, the maternal relatives are the most honored.

Han women in Yongshui do not step out of their chambers after the age of fourteen. Men have a capping ceremony at the age of twenty, with a banquet for guests. Relatives give names and do not restrict gifts. The customs are simple and ancient, and etiquette is still preserved.

Setting Off on Campaign 151

— A member of the Youth Aid-Horse Corps

(13) Passing Tianjin

Sangyuan is a town on the border of Yan (Hebei Province) and Lu (Shandong Province). Before the train started, I wanted to pay attention to the characteristics of this exotic landscape. How could I know that when we set off from Licheng, it was the first watch of the night when everything was silent. Coincidentally, that night my soul suffered under the iron hooves of Jinan. Therefore, I didn't even know when the train passed this important town of Sangyuan. What a pity!

I slept on the train for a night and sat on the train for a whole half-day the next day. From my own point of view, I can infer the common feelings of everyone. I think the comrades in this compartment are probably helpless against these boring times. The train's limbs suddenly stopped and then suddenly ran, indicating the names of places to us, as if to tell us not to forget this magnificent journey.

Suddenly, the whistle roared again as before. After a while, the two big characters "Tianjin" flashed across our eyes. The train slowly stopped as if it were wilting. At this time, the sound of people outside the window was noisy. Sturdy porters kindly greeted passengers in Northern Mandarin. There were also compatriots at the station welcoming us. But because we had to move forward immediately, we could only thank them for their enthusiasm.

This place is a famous commercial center in our country. Construction and transportation are well-equipped. Imperialists have long coveted it. Therefore, both sides of the Bai River are rented by foreign countries. Recently, the tyranny has been harassing Tianjin, relying on the land we rented to him to cause trouble. So, this misfortune of Tianjin is also the root of our own trouble.

Talking About Stones 152

— Feng Jia

The Yuhua Terrace stones in Nanjing have five colors. When placed in water, they are fresh, lively, and translucent, making them very lovely. During the late Qing Dynasty, every time there was an autumn exam, the vendors lining up in Maiyuan Street waiting for buyers were too numerous to count. The most precious ones were those with colors on the stone surface that formed the shapes of people or living things.

The Moso Mountain in Lijiang produces nephrite. The locals dig holes to extract it. When it first comes out, it is like gypsum, but it hardens when exposed to wind. Some look like jasper or agarwood jade, and they are very bright and transparent. The softer ones are like the stones from Qing Tian and Shou Shan caves. They are too brittle to be carved into seals but can be carved into wine vessels and water droppers. They can be given as local gifts and are called nephrite. There is also a type of black jade that is very solid. When it first comes out, it is green, but when it is touched with oil or sweaty hands, it becomes as black as lacquer. It is made into prayer beads and called Beifeng stone.

In Fujian, there is a Qingshan Mountain, which is the gateway to Putian. It produces "Xiangsi" stones, also called "male-female" stones. They are shaped like almonds and are white. When split, they have patterns inside. When placed on a plate and sprinkled with water, the two halves stand facing each other and then merge into one.

Meizhou in Fujian is located in the middle of the sea, with a circumference of over eighty miles. It is northeast of Chongwu and southeast of Pinghai, facing Ryukyu. The mountains produce black and white "Bo" stones, which can be used as chess pieces.

Seventy miles north of Lingbi County in Anhui Province, there is Qing Stone Mountain. (寰宇記 "Records of the Universe") says, "It is forty miles southwest of Xiapie County. Now, the Qing stones are taken to supply the Music Bureau. The floating Qing stones from Sishui in the Tribute of Yu are from here." Zhao Xihu wrote: Lingbi stones are found deep in the mountains, and they are only visible when dug. They are the color of lacquer, with thin white patterns like jade. They make a clear and far-reaching sound when struck. They cannot be scratched with a sharp knife. Fake ones are often made by dyeing Taihu stones.

Taihu stones are very precious. They have white patterns and make a slight sound when struck. Their exquisite and transparent parts are formed by water erosion, not by human work. However, genuine products are not easy to see. Forgers often wash and scrub them in water, removing their sharp edges. After several years, they sell them for a great profit. Only those with knowledge can distinguish them. Genuine ones have stone bones that have been eroded by waves. Over time, holes are formed naturally. Because they are in the water, they are difficult to transport.

Nowadays, people pile stones in gardens to create small mountains, which are called rockeries. The Sanfu Huangtu ("Maps and Records of the Three Capital Areas") records that Liang Xiaowang built the Tu Garden. The garden had Bai Ling Mountain, with rocks with names like "Fucun Stone," "Luo Yuan Rock," and "Xi Long Hillock." It also quotes the "Xijiuyiyi" saying that Yuan Guanghan, a wealthy man from Maoling, built a garden at the foot of the North Mountain, four miles east-west and five miles north-south. He channeled flowing water into it and constructed mountains with stones, over ten zhang high and extending for several miles. According to this, rockeries existed as early as the Han Dynasty. (Pi Rixiu's poem) "Children are not allowed to startle the secluded birds; medicinal herbs must be planted on the rockery."

The most precious Tian Huang stone is deep yellow like a ripe chestnut. The best ones are slightly transparent and have a crystalline radish shape. It is extremely precious when used for seals. Mao Qiling's "Hou Guan Shi Lu" ("Record of Stones Observed Later") calls the Tian Keng the best among the old collections of Shou Shan stones. It is also written as "Tian Huang" or "Tian Huang."

"Hua Ru Shi" (化乳石) is a type of pattern stone produced on Mount Tiantai Baohua. Its color is like tortoiseshell, and it is lustrous, firm, and clean. It can be used for books and paintings. (See "Tiantai Mountain Zhi" (天台山志).) Wang Mian of the late Yuan Dynasty first used "Hua Ru Shi" (化乳石) to carve seals, which was the beginning of stone seals. (See "Qixiu Leigao" (七修類稿).)

North of Zhaoqing City is the Seven Star Crags. Its stones are white and as lustrous as jade, and they can be used to make playthings.

Northern Travel Images and Others (6) 153

— Yao Sufeng

An Autobiography by Movie Star Hu Die (Butterfly Wu)

After several days of traveling to Beiping (Beijing), I was mentally exhausted, but once I arrived in Beiping, the surprised and delighted feelings made me forget all the uncomfortable impressions. This is a kind of psychological change. Beiping is such a lovable place! Seeing the buildings in Beiping, I despise those eighty- or ninety-story foreign buildings in Shanghai. Listening to the local accent of the people in Beiping, I don't want to listen to the singing in foreign talkies anymore. I haven't been to Beiping for many years, and the changes in Beiping are certainly not few, but when I think of my past travels, I can still vaguely recognize them.

Work Begins After we identified the houses and negotiated everything, we started working. Mr. Hong Shen and Mr. Zhang Shichuan set a timetable, and we all followed it. We had to get up at six o'clock every morning and couldn't finish work until four o'clock in the afternoon. It seemed busier and more disciplined than in Shanghai. However, at that time, the footsteps of our group were almost regarded as a rare pleasure by the people of Beiping. Not to mention that during the filming of location shots, the audience outside the open-air theater was often standing full (not seated full), even outside our residence, the porters were often overwhelmed. But as for ourselves, in addition to busy work, we can no longer use unnecessary social interactions to reduce our rest time. Although many unfamiliar friends came to us to talk or take pictures, we always politely declined, "living in seclusion and keeping things simple" -- this was a plan that was decided before we even came.

Record of Two Stories of Military Life (20) 154

— Master of the Seeking Happiness Studio

Chapter 3: Yu and Liang Arrive Together, Causing the Feast to Break Up; Yin and Xing Avoid Each Other, Unknowing Who Lost the Enamel Box. When An Yutian saw that she was so unhurried, with so much delay and preparation before leaving, he was secretly suffering in his heart. But he couldn't go against her, so he had to order the tea boy to fetch water quickly. After a while, the water was brought. Liang Xiaoyun rolled up her sleeves, revealing a pair of jade arms like snow lotuses. She went to the washstand and slowly wrung the towel to wash her face. Then she washed her hands carefully again. But she still wasn't done. She then took out a small, crystalline, golden powder box from a handbag. She gently pressed the mechanism on the lid. With a "chi" sound, it opened, revealing a small round mirror. She then took out a small pink powder puff from the box and dipped it in some foreign fragrant powder. She kept rubbing it on her delicate cheeks that seemed to break with a touch. The skills were truly indescribably exquisite. If it were a normal day with nothing to do, it would be a pleasure for An Yutian to quietly watch the beauty put on makeup. But today, he was restless in his heart, thinking that Li Wenxia was about to barge in. He really didn't have the leisure to enjoy this eye candy in detail. One eye watched her slowly and leisurely taking care of her own makeup, but she didn't care how anxious others were in their hearts, as if she was deliberately wasting time just to make things difficult for others. He wanted to reach out and do the delicate work roughly, quickly finishing it so she could pack up and leave. But that was just what he thought. Not only did he not dare to boldly overstep and do the job for her, but even if he wanted to impudently urge her, his teeth would be chattering and he couldn't even hum. His other eye had nothing to do, so he often peeked at the alarm clock on the desk. He saw that it was taking the opportunity to make things difficult for him. The long and short hands were moving faster than any other day. In the blink of an eye, Liang Xiaoyun had only done half of her makeup, but the clock was about to move half an hour. This half hour was enough time for Li Wenxia to hire a car from the Normal University to get here. An Yutian secretly cried that everything was ruined, completely ruined. This time, the enemies were bound to run into each other, unavoidably. He reluctantly steeled his heart, resolved to deal with both sides. At this critical moment, seeing that this three-way love tragedy was about to begin, he was preparing to go on stage and join the performance. It was useless to just be alarmed and anxious.
