Small Forum

A Small Lesson from Watching a Movie Preview 155

For a long time, I haven't gone to see movie previews. The other day, ×× Film Company kindly sent me two invitation tickets because their first talkie "......" had been completed. They had a preview at the Carlton Theater. I was moved by curiosity, so yesterday (24th) at 11:00 AM (the invitation ticket said 11:30, but I arrived half an hour early), I drove there.

At that time, the American sailors were also at the Carlton, holding their "......" worship service. It hadn't finished yet. The invited comrades (not the party comrades, but the theater-watching comrades) and their lovers ...... had to wait outside the door, chatting about their love stories.

Finally, with a "Amen" sound, the double doors opened, and the men and women comrades swarmed in, each fighting for a place. After the seats were set and the line of sight was concentrated, they hoped for the blessing of eye pleasure. Unexpectedly, after stretching their necks for a long time, Mr. Zhou came out from behind the curtain. First, he reported the difficulties in making the film "......" and the economics of the preparation time. Then he said:

"I am sorry that several segments of the '......' film are still being reviewed in the capital and have not yet been obtained. Since they have not yet been obtained, we cannot open it today. Please come to the ×× Theater on time tomorrow, and we will be honored by your presence."

Hearing this report, the comrades all hung their heads in disappointment, clicking their tongues in dissatisfaction. But what I don't understand is, since the film hasn't arrived in Shanghai, why issue invitation tickets in advance? Even if it's for economic and time reasons, issuing them in advance, then by the time of the opening, they must have known the film hadn't arrived. Why didn't the company report it earlier, so as to avoid the comrades waiting for a long time, resulting in great disappointment?

Moreover, government agencies do things based on their "happiness". When they are "happy," they immediately review. When they are "unhappy," delaying for ten or half a month is not rare. If they still haven't gotten it now, and we go there tomorrow, running in vain again, what can we say?

Although this is just a trivial matter, it doesn't matter if we don't see it. But the way Chinese people do things often makes people lose faith. This can be seen here. After Mr. Zhou finished his report, another gentleman reported:

"Gentlemen, please sit down and don't get up. The invitation tickets received today must be returned one by one." After the report was finished, the tickets were started to be returned.

Unexpectedly, some comrades didn't listen to the report and swarmed forward, surrounding the ticket clerk, like the situation on Wangping Street. Seeing this situation, the ticket clerk shouted "No issuing!" "No issuing!" incessantly. As a result, the "radicals" achieved their goal, and the "moderates" were completely disappointed.

Seeing this situation, I couldn't help but have a deep impression. Chinese people not keeping order and not caring about public welfare has become their second nature. So everywhere, we can see facts of them destroying order and disregarding public morality occurring.

Therefore, I got a small lesson. People who destroy order and disregard public morality completely achieve their rights and goals, while people who generally abide by the rules and respect order are completely disappointed. Assuming that the same thing happens again in the future, the people who follow order, learning from the past, will also be assimilated.

Ah! Although this is a small matter in a movie theater, I'm afraid it's still a microcosm of the entire China?

Public Literature and Art

Mr. Bitter Silk 156

A road repair worker, one day a sudden disaster came from nowhere.

Carrying mud and stones in a bustling throng, soldiers and floods came one after another.

Twenty or thirty people strove together, their parents dead, their homes broken.

Only one person was slow and listless. His wife and children were small and weak, lamenting pathetically.

The foreman was furious at first sight, cursing him countless times.

"Pig's intestines, killing blank bonehead! If you want to enjoy the good life, sit at home!"

The person cursed walked slowly, tears streaming down his face before the foreman,

"I was born as a scholar, writing and reading in a school,

Until I graduated from high school, at the age of twenty without any other skill.

I use a shoulder pole and not a pen, shoulders being utterly powerless,

But I beg you, sir, don't be angry, I'm only speaking the truth.

To collect scattered odds, to go to other lands, seeking food and clothing in sorrow and fear,

Three years and a thousand miles, coming to Shanghai to make my way.

Shanghai's golden streets were everywhere, but I lament it's hard to get a hold of,

A kindly old man, took me in at the Bureau (Public Works Bureau) with a name card,

And finding him his old son, the road was assigned for me to be a worker.

The foreman hearing these words, being calmed and not angry,

I can feed my family, But to the end, all I can expect is death."

Replacing the curses with soothing words, "I heard your story and am so sorry."

"I will beg the sir will show patience, Take a few days off to rest,"

"Honing your muscles to repay his kindness. You are really Mr. Bitter."

Public Science

Talking About Carbon Dioxide - Meng Fu 157

Carbon dioxide is a compound of carbon or carbonaceous substances and oxygen. Its chemical name is carbon dioxide (Carbon Dioxide) and its formula is (Co2). This gas is commonly found in the atmosphere, but not in large quantities. Roughly, in rural and open areas, the air contains four parts per ten thousand, while in urban and populated areas, the air contains roughly one percent.

The combustion of all fuels, the respiration of living things, and the decay of animals and plants can all produce this gas. Moreover, in volcanic areas, it erupts from the strata. Here are a few examples: near Naples in Italy, there is a cave that emits carbon dioxide. In Yellowstone Park in the Americas, there is a Death Gulch, where living things suffocate and die upon entering because it contains a large amount of carbon dioxide. However, although nature constantly produces carbon dioxide, the amount contained in the air remains roughly the same. This is because plant leaves use sunlight to perform a kind of assimilation, which decomposes the absorbed carbon dioxide into carbon and oxygen, absorbs the carbon to form starch and carbohydrates, and releases fresh oxygen. Therefore, plants are of great importance to human life.

Carbon dioxide is a colorless and odorless gas that causes suffocation but is not poisonous. It also has a characteristic that lime water can combine with carbon dioxide to produce a milky white precipitate. Therefore, we can use this method to test for carbon dioxide: cover a candle flame with a glass, and after a few minutes, pour clear lime water into it, and then shake it vigorously, and the clear lime water will gradually turn milky white. Or, you can exhale your breath into clear lime water, and you will get the same result. If you want to obtain a large amount of carbon dioxide using chemical methods, you only need to inject dilute hydrochloric acid (this acid is commonly used) into marble (i.e., calcium carbonate Calcium Carbonate), and you will get it.

Carbon dioxide has a wide range of uses. I have written down the common and important ones below:

(1) Beverages丨The soda water that relieves the heat in summer uses high pressure to dissolve a large amount of carbon dioxide in the liquid, or soda water is made from baking soda and citric acid. Beer and other beverages also use carbon dioxide as a refreshing and beneficial drink.

(2) Fire Extinguishing丨Fire extinguishers sold on the market are made using the principle that carbon dioxide can isolate oxygen and does not support combustion. The general method is as follows: a small bottle containing concentrated sulfuric acid is suspended in a solution of heavy soda (Sodium bicarbonate). If a fire occurs, quickly invert the fire extinguisher, and the small bottle will break, the two liquids will combine to generate carbon dioxide, and the gas can be used to spray out the liquid. Sometimes, even if the fire is large, this device can be effective. A certain fire extinguisher manufacturing company in Shanghai has carried out multiple on-site tests in public, and the results have been very satisfactory. Science is truly omnipotent!

(3) Liquid Carbon Dioxide丨If the temperature is lowered and the pressure is increased, carbon dioxide will become a colorless liquid. It can be loaded into steel cylinders and supplied to people who manufacture soda water and other beverages. Recently, liquid carbon dioxide has been loaded into steel cylinders as fire extinguishers. Then, the carbon dioxide is still transformed into a gas and vented, because when the mechanism is opened, the pressure is reduced and the temperature is increased. Therefore, the liquid still returns to being a gas. In Europe and the United States, some electrical factories, cotton powder factories, and ships have used this device. (The End) Street Sociology

Flow! Cry! One factory! 158

Every day, for work, I have to pass through the area of North Sichuan Road Bund Sima Road. I often see beggars without feet below the shinbones, regardless of the weather. They flow and cry, "Gentlemen! Ladies! Do good deeds!" Their voice is sad and miserable! People passing by intentionally or unintentionally throw one or two copper coins into their broken baskets. They still push the broken baskets and flow! Cry! These tragic sounds and tragic sights are forever never heard nor seen by the gentlemen and ladies who glide past in cars.

In these tragic sounds, we have to ask why their feet are gone?

No more than three ways:

(1) Chopped off as a cruel punishment for a crime, or slowly rotted away by cruel punishments (such as standing in a lime bucket ......)!

(2) Blasted away by the ruthless bullets of guns and artillery during wartime!

(3) Disabled due to an extremely unfortunate accident!

If the disability was obtained in (1), then how cruel is this punishment! For the sake of respecting the complete health of human limbs, there is a real need for rectification. If it was obtained in (2), then how cold is society to the heroes who endure wind and rain for the country and the race!

Shanghai is a place of international concern, allowing these disabled people to flow and cry on the streets is enough to expose the weakness of the municipality. A disabled people's home should be urgently established to settle these miserable people who are on the verge of death.

East South West North

The Life of a Worker, Big Brother 159

There are three classes in society. The propertied class naturally lives a superior life. The working class can also manage. But it is the white-collar class that is neither up nor down that feels the most difficulty. Hypocritical appearances cannot be exposed. The meager monthly salary is even less than that of a worker. After deducting household expenses, there are still personal consumption and social expenses, so there is always no surplus. It is difficult to add a piece of clothing without the risk of living beyond one's means. If the heavens do not bless you and you get sick, medical expenses can only be obtained from debt. If you break your rice bowl and lack recommendations, or for the sake of saving face, you are unwilling to stoop to becoming a worker, then you will inevitably fall into decline and destitution. A worker with a skill does not have to worry about finding a place to eat. This is the advantage of a worker in making a living.

Workers in China originally had no status. They have always been regarded as "trivial pursuits," so their lives are the simplest. Four or five unmarried people rent a loft together. Married people rent a pavilion or back building for four or five yuan. Food costs four or five yuan, and clothing costs three or four yuan. That is all the monthly expenses. If the monthly income is 20 yuan, there is already a surplus. They live in humble dwellings, eat poorly, and wear shabby clothes, and no one cares about it. (People would say that the white-collar class is having bad luck.) However, since the revolution in 1927, workers have occupied a considerable position, and wages have increased a lot. Ordinary workers can earn more than 40 yuan a month. There are still a few factories where workers are demanding pay increases. Frankly speaking, the work of workers is very hard. Who doesn't need a pleasant and comfortable life? Some of them have rich experience, high skills, and many family members, and they feel insecure because their wages are too low. It is hoped that the capitalists will consider the situation and increase their wages. There are also quite a few workers who have no family burden; or even if they have a surplus, they spend it on improper expenses, and therefore feel that their wages are not enough. Let me give a few examples:

(1) A certain worker's income is still acceptable, and his household expenses are extremely frugal, with half of his monthly income left over, but he often goes to gambling dens, resulting in heavy debts.

(2) A certain worker is single and has no family burden, but he likes fancy clothes and decorations. When he goes out after work, he looks like a young gentleman, so he cannot make ends meet.

(3) A certain worker likes to patronize prostitutes and has a mistress.

(4) Some factory workers spend money recklessly after receiving their wages, not even waiting overnight, and have nothing left.

(5) A certain female worker's family situation is average. Her monthly salary is enough to support herself, but her attire is like that of a rich woman.

What I said above is indeed the weakness of some workers, not slandering them, and even less is it intentional to criticize them. Because I have discovered the above-mentioned weaknesses, I cannot bear to remain silent, so I have spoken frankly and unceremoniously. If you read it and correct your mistakes if you have them, and strive to do better if you don't, this is my personal hope, and it is also the happiness of the country and society!

Shanghai Stories

Shanghai Stories (18) Compiled and Translated by Zhou Rong 160

× French Troops Assist Government Troops in Attacking the City (Continued)

The Small Swords Society had set up artillery positions at what is now Chenjia Wooden Bridge. Larer ordered them to be dismantled, but the Swords Society refused. Larer then joined forces with the government officers to capture the county seat. They first attacked the north gate, near the present-day Catholic Church on Yangjingbang. The French troops attacked fiercely, destroying a corner of the city wall, but because they did not receive assistance from the government troops, their efforts failed. Two French officers were killed, four were wounded, and thirty-two soldiers were wounded and seven were killed. After this battle, the government troops built a long wall from the Bund to the intersection of Henan Road, across the large wooden bridge over Yangjingbang (i.e., Chenjia Wooden Bridge), to cut off traffic between the city and the concession. The city was cut off from outside aid and became increasingly difficult to sustain. On February 17, 1854, the Swords Society withdrew from the county seat, which had been occupied for seventeen months. When the government troops entered the city, the order was in great chaos. The eastern part of the city was completely destroyed by fire. The government troops captured the bandits and immediately beheaded them, and the slaughter was not small.
